"Direct Marketing doesn't w o r k "
T h e r e a r e 2 f o r m s o f m a r k e t i n g a t play... m e a s u r a b l e results f r o m y o u r m a r k e t i n g . . . a n d n o n - m e a s u r a b l e results f r o m
your marketing.
I m a g e a d v e r t i s i n g , o r n o n - m e a s u r a b l e m a r k e t i n g , is designed t o b u i l d g e n e r a l a w a r e n e s s o f y o u r o f f e r i n g a n d y o u r
message... a n d n o t a b o u t specific results o n a day-by-day basis. T h e r e have b e e n m a n y m u l t i - m i l l i o n (and b i l l i o n ) d o l l a r
e m p i r e s b u i l t exclusively o n t h i s f o r m o f m a r k e t i n g ( f i r m s t h a t have n e v e r used direct m a r k e t i n g t e c h n i q u e s ) .
BUT... the average entrepreneur doesn't have deep enough pockets
to sustain imagine-only advertising.

T h e y n e e d t o k n o w right n o w w h a t ad is w o r k i n g o r sales l e t t e r is p u l l i n g i n clients - a n d w h i c h a r e n ' t .
W i t h o u t t h i s k n o w l e d g e - t h e y w i l l q u i c k l y go b r o k e .
W h e n t h e y k n o w w h i c h ad, placed i n w h i c h m e d i a p u b l i c a t i o n o r w e b s i t e , w o r k s a n d m a k e s t h e m m o n e y - t h e y t h e n
have a s y s t e m t h e y can r e p e a t u n t i l it stops w o r k i n g .
T h e y can m e a s u r e exactly w h a t each n e w lead costs t h e m t o g e n e r a t e - a n d h o w m u c h t h e y n e e d t o invest i n e a c h real
lead t o c o n v e r t t h e m t o a paying c u s t o m e r - a n d t h e n h o w m u c h t o c o n v e r t e a c h o n e - t i m e c u s t o m e r t o a r e p e a t buyer.
If y o u have b e e n r e a d i n g T h e R e n e g a d e Club N e w s l e t t e r f o r s o m e t i m e n o w , y o u have s e e n m u l t i p l e e x a m p l e s a n d
t e m p l a t e s f o r c r e a t i n g q u a l i t y leads, a n d t h e n c o n v e r t i n g t h o s e leads i n t o paying c u s t o m e r s .
This knowledge is pure gold when you know it.

A n d yes, d i r e c t m a r k e t i n g DOES w o r k - a n d can be p r o v e n r i g h t d o w n t o t h e p e n n y h o w w e l l it d o e s w o r k . Y o u c a n n o t
say t h a t a b o u t i m a g e o r b r a n d a w a r e n e s s c a m p a i g n s ( t h e exact a m o u n t i t m a d e f o r t h e business c a n n e v e r b e
m e a s u r e d as t h e y have n o w a y o f m e a s u r i n g i t ) .
"No one will read all those words
- people are different now and don't read as much"

T h e n to match this balance w i t h your exact target market.

Only through testing will you know
w h a t the right amount of w o r d s is.

A n d a s s u m i n g y o u k n o w is t h e s u r e s t w a y t o kill y o u r m a r k e t i n g r e s u l t s . Y o u d o n ' t k n o w w h a t y o u r c l i e n t s
w a n t - until y o u ask t h e m ( t h r o u g h m a r k e t i n g tests). T h e y will o f t e n tell y o u t h e y w a n t o n e t h i n g , b u t will
s h o w different responses w h e n tested.
It is c o m p l e t e l y u p t o y o u t o f i n d t h e p e r f e c t m a t c h .
"There is a magical percentage conversion rate"

T h i s is q u i t e c o m m o n . " I n e e d a 2% c o n v e r s i o n r a t e - a n y t h i n g b e l o w t h a t i s u n a c c e p t a b l e . " M y q u e s t i o n t o
t h e m is " W H Y ? "
A n y p e r s o n f a m i l i a r w i t h m a r k e t i n g k n o w s t h a t t h e r e a l m o n e y is i n t h e b a c k e n d p r o d u c t s a n d s e r v i c e s y o u
sell t o y o u r clients. If y o u a r e selling a $ 2 5 b o o k - y o u w i l l n e v e r g e t rich (or m a k e a n y real m o n e y ) w i t h o u t
s o m e t h i n g else t o sell.
You M U S T have s o m e t h i n g else - a t a higher price p o i n t t o sell.
And if you k n o w that 10% of your book buyers will buy your $1,000 backend offer - w h o cares if you lose
m o n e y or break even on the book sale.

In o t h e r w o r d s - c o n c e r n y o u r s e l f less a b o u t t h e c o n v e r s i o n r a t e - a n d s t a r t w o r r y i n g a b o u t t h e P R O F I T y o u
m a k e . If y o u d o n ' t have a system i n place t o u p t h e profit y o u m a k e after t h e initial sale ( t o a n e w client)
t h e n a 3 % c o n v e r s i o n rate ( w h i c h is v e r y g o o d o n it's o w n ) possibly m e a n s n o t h i n g o t h e r t h a n t h e fact y o u
are g o i n g b r o k e fast selling y o u r $ 2 5 b o o k .
D o y o u h o n e s t l y t h i n k t h a t a c o m p a n y s e l l i n g m i l l i o n dollar, o c e a n f r o n t , a n d gated c o m m u n i t y h o m e s is
concerned about a 1 % response rate t o their mailer?
T h e y are m o r e concerned w i t h t h e quality o f people t h e y attract and t h e f o l l o w u p system t h e y use t o m a k e
sure t h e lead buys.
They may only get a 0 . 1 % response rate to their mailer
- but it makes t h e m a million dollars.

w o r k f o r y o u t o o i f y o u g i v e i t a c h a n c e a n d s o m e p a t i e n c e . CONT'D - Page 7

Five hated words you never want to hear
Quick, w h a t are t h e five w o r d s y o u n e v e r w a n t t o h e a r w h e n selling? T h a t ' s right. T h e five m o s t
h a t e d w o r d s in selling are, " H a v e t o t h i n k a b o u t it." W h y ? Because it so o f t e n m e a n s t h e d e a t h o f a
sale - right at t h e v e r y e n d - after all y o u r h a r d w o r k . A f t e r y o u r m e e t i n g s . Y o u r r e s e a r c h . Y o u r
m e a s u r i n g . Your design w o r k . Your r e t u r n visits t o t h e c u s t o m e r w h e n t h e y r e q u e s t changes. After
e v e r y t h i n g y o u ' v e d o n e t o m a k e s u r e t h a t t h e client gets a perfect s o l u t i o n , a n d y o u get a p e r f e c t sale. A n d
w h a t are y o u left w i t h ? U n c e r t a i n t y . D i s a p p o i n t m e n t . Frustration. O f t e n r e s e n t m e n t . S o m e t i m e s e v e n anger,
because y o u m a y very w e l l feel used and a b u s e d .
O n e t h i n g y o u ' r e n o t l e f t w i t h is c l a r i t y . Y o u d o n ' t k n o w w h a t h a p p e n e d . W a s i t p r i c e ? W a s i t b u d g e t o r
t e r m s ? W a s it s o m e w o r r y t h a t d i d n ' t s h o w up w h e n y o u w e r e qualifying? W a s it u n e a s i n e s s a b o u t l e a v i n g
t h e i r p r e s e n t p r o v i d e r ? W a s i t f e a r o f d i s r u p t i o n a n d l o s s o f p r o d u c t i o n w h i l e y o u r s o l u t i o n is i n s t a l l e d o r
i m p l e m e n t e d ? W h o k n o w s ? Often, e v e n the client doesn't know...they m a y have said t h e y need t o t h i n k
a b o u t i t w i t h o u t e v e n t h i n k i n g a b o u t w h a t t h e y w e r e g o i n g t o t h i n k a b o u t . W h o k n o w s ? T h i s is c l e a r l y a
situation y o u w a n t t o avoid. So here's how.
Use t h e "C" w o r d t o w o r k t h r o u g h closing-stage objections
O f t e n y o u r t r i a l c l o s e w i l l r e v e a l t h a t t h e p r o s p e c t is s t i l l n o t r e a d y t o b u y - f o r s o m e r e a s o n t h a t m a y n o t b e
k n o w n t o e i t h e r y o u o r t h e c l i e n t . T h i s is w h e n y o u h e a r m a n y p r o s p e c t s say, "Til have to think about it."
W h e n t h i s h a p p e n s , y o u m u s t n o t l e t t h e m g o a n d t h i n k a b o u t i t alone. T h e k e y is t o u s e t h e " C " w o r d
("Collaborate") t o help t h e prospect identify t h e i r real c o n c e r n - and help t h e m deal w i t h it effectively. Y o u
m u s t n o t a s k a q u e s t i o n l i k e , "When should I get back to you?" If y o u d o y o u c o u l d b e g i v i n g u p t h e s a l e .
Instead, h a n g in t h e r e , and collaborate w i t h y o u r prospect.
T h e k e y p o i n t is t h i s : T h e d i f f e r e n c e b e t w e e n " c l o s i n g " a n d " l o s i n g " a s a l e is t h e l e t t e r " C . " A n d " C " s t a n d s f o r
" C o l l a b o r a t e . " C o l l a b o r a t e m e a n s t o " c o - l a b o u r , " t o " w o r k t o g e t h e r , " a n d t h i s is t h e k e y t o y o u r s u c c e s s .
Think back to the sales process for clues

T h i n k b a c k t o o b j e c t i o n s t h a t s u r f a c e d e a r l i e r i n y o u r d i s c u s s i o n s . I f t h e f i t is r i g h t ( m e a n i n g t h e p r o s p e c t
w o u l d gain a significant b e n e f i t f r o m b u y i n g n o w , and f r o m b u y i n g f r o m y o u ) , t h e n t h e r e m u s t be an
o u t s t a n d i n g i s s u e t h a t is s t i l l a c o n c e r n .
Often, w e will hear concerns early o n - a b o u t price or affordability, for e x a m p l e - but not pay close e n o u g h
a t t e n t i o n t o t h e m - or feel t h a t w e ' v e resolved t h e m w h e n w e really haven't. T h e n t h e y re-appear h e r e at t h e
c l o s i n g s t a g e - i n t h e f o r m o f w o r d s l i k e , "We're going to have to think about it," t h a t c a n d e s t r o y a p e r f e c t
sale.
T o f i n d o u t , f o r b o t h y o u r b e n e f i t a n d t h e c l i e n t ' s , ask
s p e c i f i c q u e s t i o n s . A s i m p l e q u e s t i o n s u c h as, "Are you
thinking about the budget, Chris?" c o u l d b r i n g t h e i s s u e
o u t in t h e o p e n , and give y o u a c h a n c e t o w o r k t h r o u g h it
together.
For e x a m p l e , y o u m a y be able t o reconfigure t h e s o l u t i o n
y o u h a v e d e s i g n e d f o r t h e c l i e n t t o r e d u c e its c o s t . O r
extend t e r m s . Or start w i t h a partial solution. A n d build
t h e t o t a l s o l u t i o n o v e r time. E v e n i f y o u g u e s s w r o n g
a b o u t t h e issue, y o u r q u e s t i o n could p r o m p t y o u r

F o r m e r b u s i n e s s j o u r n a l i s t , N e i l G o d i n ( a . k . a . T h e T u r n a r o u n d Guy®) is p u b lisher of "Marketing Dangerously," the world's only marketing and sales "idea
s e r v i c e " f o r b u s i n e s s b u i l d e r s , a n d a u t h o r o f " S e l l i n g in t h e ( C o m f o r t )
Z o n e " (available at A m a z o n and other outlets). A s a speaker Neil has
p r e s e n t e d t o m o r e t h a n 3 0 0 , 0 0 0 b u s i n e s s p e o p l e f r o m c o a s t t o c o a s t in
Canada and the United States. A s a marketing and sales consultant and
coach, he h a s w o r k e d with m a n y major c o m p a n i e s , including Shell, F o r d ,
T h e R o y a l Bank, Telus, D u n & Bradstreet, S u b w a y and M c D o n a l d s , but
w o r k s m a i n l y w i t h s m a l l e r i n d e p e n d - e n t b u s i n e s s e s - a n d h e s p e c i a l i z e s in
t u r n a r o u n d m a r k e t i n g w o r k w i t h s m a l l t o m i d - s i z e c o m p a n i e s in c r i s i s . In
these turnaround cases, sales a l w a y s h a v e to be doubled or tripled—
i m m e d i a t e l y — a n d a t m i n i m a l c o s t . In h i s s p e a k i n g , w r i t i n g a n d c o a c h i n g
work, Neil shares these turnaround ideas with o w n e r s of healthy businesses
w h o j u s t w a n t t o r a m p u p t h e i r s a l e s . If t h i s d e s c r i b e s y o u , t h e n N e i l
w e l c o m e s y o u r call or e m a i l . H i s s t r a t e g i e s c a n help y o u i n c r e a s e y o u r s a l e s
- rapidly - n o m a t t e r w h a t b u s i n e s s y o u ' r e in, or w h a t condition y o u r
b u s i n e s s ( o r t h e e c o n o m y ) is i n . Y o u c a n r e a c h N e i l a t 1 . 8 0 0 . 5 6 3 . I D E A

prospect t o disclose s o m e o t h e r concern. Either w a y y o u give y o u r s e l f an o p p o r t u n i t y t o c o n t i n u e t h e collaborative
e f f o r t , a n d g e t t h e s a l e c l o s e d - n o w ! T h e p o i n t is t h a t i f y o u i d e n t i f y t h e a c t u a l i s s u e , y o u a n d y o u r c l i e n t c a n w o r k

c o n c e r n s , t h e t r u t h is t h a t t h e y c a n ' t w o r k t h r o u g h t h e i r p r o b l e m s u c c e s s f u l l y w i t h o u t y o u .
Your goal is to close the sale - n o w !

R e m e m b e r this: A n y delay - for any reason - can take t h e prospect's a t t e n t i o n a w a y f r o m t h e purchasing process,
a n d y o u m a y n e v e r g e t i t b a c k . Y o u k n o w t h i s is h a p p e n i n g w h e n y o u m a k e f o l l o w u p calls t o t h e c l i e n t t h a t a r e n o t
r e t u r n e d . W o r s e , i f t h e p r o s p e c t is r e a d y , w i l l i n g a n d a b l e t o b u y n o w - a n d y o u d o n ' t c l o s e t h e s a l e - t h e n y o u a r e
in clear and p r e s e n t d a n g e r o f l e t t i n g t h e m slip i n t o t h e h a n d s o f c o m p e t i t o r s .
This can m e a n t h a t y o u r hard w o r k - y o u r i n t e r v i e w i n g ; y o u r m e a s u r i n g ; y o u r design; y o u r great s o l u t i o n s t o t h e i r
design issues - will n o w b e used t o t r y and get a better deal e l s e w h e r e . O u c h .
W h e n t h e s e things h a p p e n y o u give u p a sale t h a t s h o u l d have b e e n closed. T h e prospect loses t h e o p p o r t u n i t y t o
b e n e f i t f r o m w h a t y o u o f f e r . Y o u b o t h l o s e t h e time a n d e f f o r t t h a t w e n t i n t o t h e s a l e s p r o c e s s . Y o u l o s e t h e l i f e time v a l u e o f t h e p r o s p e c t i n t e r m s o f t h e i r r e p e a t a n d r e f e r r a l b u s i n e s s . A n d y o u l o s e r e v e n u e b e c a u s e o f t h e l o s t
opportunity. Ouch again.
Working with just one decision maker is a set up for failure

W h e n t w o ( o r m o r e ) p e o p l e w i l l b e m a k i n g t h e final d e c i s i o n - a n d y o u m e e t w i t h j u s t o n e - y o u m a y b e s e t t i n g
y o u r s e l f up t o fail. W h e n this "one-legged" sales s i t u a t i o n crops up, y o u r prospect has a bullet-proof, built-in
o b j e c t i o n t o c l o s i n g t h e s a l e . T h e i r a b s o l u t e o u t is t h e e x c u s e t h a t t h e y h a v e t o t a l k i t o v e r w i t h t h e i r p a r t n e r . S o ,
w h e n setting a p p o i n t m e n t s b e sure t o qualify w h o will m a k e the decision, and if t w o are involved m a k e every effort
to meet with both.
W h a t to do w h e n you can "not" close the sale n o w

O b v i o u s l y , t h e r e w i l l s t i l l b e times w h e n y o u c a n ' t c l o s e t h e s a l e o n t h e s p o t . W h e n t h a t h a p p e n s , d o " n o t " s a y t h a t
y o u w i l l g i v e t h e m a c a l l t o f o l l o w u p . I n s t e a d , m a k e a s p e c i f i c a p p o i n t m e n t f o r a time a n d d a y w h e n y o u w i l l m e e t
or speak again.
If y o u s i m p l y c a l l t o f o l l o w u p , y o u r f o l l o w u p calls m a y v e r y w e l l b e p e r c e i v e d a s a n a n n o y a n c e ( y o u c a n i m a g i n e
y o u r p r o s p e c t t h i n k i n g , " W h y is h e c a l l i n g s o s o o n ? I s a i d w e ' d h a v e t o t h i n k a b o u t i t . " ) T h i s l e a d s t o t h e s o u l d e s t r o y i n g s i t u a t i o n w h e r e y o u first e n t e r " t h e t w i l i g h t z o n e " i n s e l l i n g - w h e r e y o u d o n ' t k n o w w h a t is h a p p e n i n g
o r w h y - and t h e n y o u r sale goes i n t o "the black hole," t h a t a w f u l place w h e r e q u o t e s and designs and all y o u r
o t h e r h a r d w o r k g o w h e n p r o s p e c t s s t o p r e t u r n i n g y o u r calls a n d e m a i l s c o m p l e t e l y .

FAST TRACK TO EBAY with Larry Yakiwczuk

A w h i l e a g o E b a y a n d t h e n a g a i n r e c e n t l y K i j i j i m a d e b i g h e a d l i n e s i n e v e r y p a p e r across
Canada! T h e y lost a court battles against R e v e n u e Canada. Because o f this r u l i n g R e v e n u e
C a n a d a w i l l b e g e t t i n g sales r e c o r d s f r o m E b a y C a n a d a f o r a l l p o w e r s e l l e r s , b o t h i n t h e past
and i n the future. T h i s could have v e r y big ramifications for m a n y Canadian sellers across the
c o u n t r y . S o i f y o u h a v e b e e n s e l l i n g o n E b a y a n d n o t d e c l a r i n g t h a t as i n c o m e o n y o u r t a x e s
then y o u m a y be the target o f a R e v e n u e Canada investigation.
N o w before I g o o n , I have t o give t h e standard disclaimer. W h a t I a m saying is m y o w n
p e r s o n a l o p i n i o n , a n d i t i s n o t m e a n t t o b e a d v i c e , a n d i t s h o u l d n o t b e acted u p o n b y a n y o n e r e a d i n g t h i s a r t i c l e . I
suggest t h a t a n y o n e r e a d i n g t h i s , c o n t a c t a s u i t a b l e p r o f e s s i o n a l i n t h e field, a n d a s k f o r t h e i r p r o f e s s i o n a l a d v i c e
o n t h e subject, p r i o r t o t a k i n g a n y a c t i o n .
F r o m m y u n d e r s t a n d i n g o f w h a t I h a v e h e a r d o r r e a d a b o u t t h e s i t u a t i o n , R e v e n u e C a n a d a is a l l o w i n g e b a y sellers
to v o l u n t a r i l y resubmit their taxes for the years i n question, 2 0 0 5 and o n w a r d . F o r certain individuals this m i g h t
be a g o o d i d e a t o c o n s i d e r .
A s a l o t o f y o u w h o k n o w m e , y o u k n o w t h a t I a m a b i t o f a c o n t r a r i a n , so m y p e r s o n a l b e l i e f is t h a t e v e r y o n e
s e l l i n g o n e b a y s h o u l d b e v o l u n t a r i l y d e c l a r i n g e v e r y p e n n y t h e y m a k e o n ebay. I a l s o p r o m o t e t h a t e v e r y e b a y
seller should also register h i m s e l f or h e r s e l f for the G S T . Yes it w i l l complicate y o u r life a bit, but I d o have m y
reasons for saying so.
F i r s t o f a l l , b y d e c l a r i n g a l l y o u r ebay sales as i n c o m e , y o u a r e n o w a b o n a fide business i n t h e e y e s o f R e v e n u e
C a n a d a . T h a t m e a n s t h a t b e s i d e s d e c l a r i n g y o u r i n c o m e , y o u a r e n o w e l i g i b l e t o a l s o declare A L L y o u r e x p e n s e s .
O f c o u r s e t h a t m e a n s n o t o n l y t h e costs y o u p a i d f o r t h e i t e m s y o u a r e s e l l i n g , b u t a l s o a l l y o u r o p e r a t i n g e x p e n s e s
as w e l l . T h i n g s s u c h as i n t e r n e t access, p h o n e l i n e s , c o m p u t e r e q u i p m e n t , d i g i t a l c a m e r a s , etc. etc. n o w a l l
become tax deducible. A l s o i f y o u operate out o f y o u r h o m e , then a percentage o f all y o u r h o m e expenses n o w
also become deductible, things like, utilities, mortgage payments, repairs a n d maintenance, a n d other such things.
A l s o c e r t a i n t r a v e l e x p e n s e s c a n a l s o n o w b e c o m e d e d u c t i b l e . M i l e a g e c h a r g e s f o r g o i n g t o t h e post o f f i c e , o r
l o c a l a u c t i o n s , o r g o i n g t o stores, c a n n o w be c l a i m e d . S a y y o u g o o n a t r i p o u t o f t o w n , stop i n t o a n a n t i q u e store
a n d b u y s o m e s m a l l i t e m t o s e l l o n ebay, keep t h e receipt, because n o w t h a t t r i p c a n b e c o m e a d e d u c t i b l e e x p e n s e .
T h e better r e c o r d s y o u k e e p t h e less l i k e l y a n y a u d i t o r w i l l c h a l l e n g e y o u r c l a i m s t o a d e d u c t i o n . A l s o i f y o u a r e
j u s t s t a r t i n g o u t , y o u c a n r u n y o u r b u s i n e s s at a loss f o r at least 3 y e a r s b e f o r e R e v e n u e C a n a d a r e q u i r e s y o u t o
s h o w a p r o f i t i n y o u r b u s i n e s s . S o t h a t i s w h y I t e l l p e o p l e t h e y s h o u l d treat t h e i r e b a y sales as a t r u e b u s i n e s s a n d
not a h o b b y .
N o w o n t o t h e G S T f o r a b i t , e v e n t h o u g h I d i d t h i s last m o n t h , I c a n n o t stress i t e n o u g h ! T h e a r g u m e n t t h a t
everyone gives is that y o u need a certain i n c o m e level before y o u are required t o register for the G S T . T h a t is true,
but y o u can v o l u n t a r i l y register even i f y o u d o not meet those i n c o m e levels, a n d I tell people t o d o so! S e l l i n g o n
e b a y a n d r e g i s t e r i n g f o r t h e G S T is a l i c e n s e t o get m o n e y f r o m t h e g o v e r n m e n t . T h e G S T i s a n e t t a x f o r
r e g i s t r a n t s . T h a t m e a n s y o u k e e p t r a c k o f t h e G S T y o u spend o n e x p e n s e s a n d f r o m t h a t y o u subtract t h e G S T t h a t
y o u c o l l e c t o n y o u r sales.
F o r m o s t b u s i n e s s e s i n C a n a d a , t h e y c o l l e c t m o r e G S T t h a n t h e y spend, so t h e y h a v e t o g i v e t h e excess a m o u n t s
t o t h e g o v e r n m e n t as a r e m i t t a n c e . B U T w h e n y o u s e l l o n E b a y , m o s t o f y o u r sales a r e g o i n g t o b e e x p o r t e d t o t h e
U S A , a n d a r e w h a t i s c a l l e d Z e r o - r a t e d sales. T h a t m e a n s y o u d o n o t c o l l e c t G S T o n sales t h a t a r e e x p o r t e d o u t o f
t h e c o u n t r y . S o as a seller, y o u c o l l e c t v e r y l i t t l e G S T o n y o u r sales ( o n l y c o l l e c t i t f o r sales w i t h i n C a n a d a ) . S o
n o w t h e G S T y o u spend o n y o u r e x p e n s e s b e c o m e s
considerably m o r e that the G S T y o u collect. T h e net result is
t h a t t h e g o v e r n m e n t sends y o u a c h e c k f o r t h e d i f f e r e n c e . I s n ' t
that sweet? I f y o u have a lot o f expenses these checks can be

auctions, his f u l l - t i m e occupation (along w i t h 2 employees

BALANCING ACT with Randall Orser
When Should You Change Course?
P l a n s are i m p o r t a n t f o r an entrepreneur. T h e y serve as a g u i d e a n d a l l o w y o i i t o f o c u s y o u r e f f o r t s
i n a d i r e c t i o n y o u h a v e d e t e r m i n e d as p r o f i t a b l e o r b e n e f i c i a l f o r y o u r start-u p. B u t s o m e t i m e s
t h i n g s change. Y o u r target d e m o g r a p h i c m a y n o t be w h a t y o u t h o u g h t i t w a s Y o u r p r o d u c t m a y n o t
w o r k i n the field as w e l l as y o u t h o u g h t . W h a t e v e r the s i t u a t i o n , y o u ' l l h a v e o ask y o u r s e l f w h e t h e r
y o u s h o u l d stay t h e course o r start p i v o t i n g .
C h a n g i n g y o u r strategy takes a l o t o f t i m e and m a k e s a l l y o u r p r e v i o u s e f f o r t m e a n i n g l e s s . A w e a k strategy c o u p l e d w i t h
c o n s i s t e n c y w i l l a l m o s t a l w a y s d o better t h a n m u l t i p l e i n t e l l i g e n t strategies t h a t n e v e r reach f r u i t i o n . O n t h e o t h e r hand,
f o r c i n g a b r o k e n strategy because that's w h a t y o u said y o u w o u l d d o can lead t o f a i l u r e . T h e t r i c k is f i g u r i n g o u t w h e n t o
change course a n d w h e n t o s t i c k t o y o u r guns.
1.

L o o k at M e a s u r a b l e M e t r i c s

B i g d r e a m s a n d concepts are great. A s a n entrepreneur, y o u ' l l need those d r e a m s a n d concepts t o d r i v e y o u f o r w a r d , t o m a k e
y o u r start-up m e a n s o m e t h i n g m o r e t h a n a m o n e y - m a k i n g m a c h i n e . H o w e v e r , t h o s e d r e a m s a n d concepts s h o u l d n o t
d e t e r m i n e w h e t h e r o r n o t y o u change y o u r plans. Y o u can't m e a s u r e t h e m , so y o u c a n n o t use t h e m t o d e t e r m i n e w h e t h e r o r
not y o u ' r e a p p r o a c h i n g y o u r goals.
W h e n d e c i d i n g o n y o u r start-up's d i r e c t i o n , t h i n k a b o u t a n u m b e r o f k e y m e t r i c s , such as y o u r c u r r e n t cash f l o w , sales
n u m b e r s , y o u r prospective c l i e n t s ; i f y o u can c o u n t i t , y o u can use i t t o j u d g e y o u r c o m p a n y ' s c u r r e n t state. U s e those
n u m b e r s t o f i g u r e o u t w h a t t o d o , a n d c o n v i n c e y o u r partners a n d i n v e s t o r s t h a t it's t h e r i g h t t h i n g t o do.
2.

Update Your Assumptions

Y o u ' r e g o i n g t o m a k e a l o t o f educated guesses t h r o u g h o u t y o u r l i f e as an entrepreneur. Y o u can gather a l l t h e i n f o r m a t i o n y o u
w a n t , b u t u l t i m a t e l y a l l y o u r p r e d i c t i o n s are j u s t t h a t — p r e d i c t i o n s . T h i n g s c a n a n d w i l l change, a n d y o u need t o adjust y o u r
assumptions accordingly.
B e g i n y o u r r e g u l a r m e e t i n g s b y l o o k i n g o v e r y o u r a s s u m p t i o n s a n d discussing w h e t h e r o r n o t t h e y t i l l h o l d w a t e r . U s e t h o s e
discussions t o figure o u t h o w y o u r plans are g o i n g .
3.

K e e p T r a c k o f Y o u r Progress

Set a r e g u l a r m e e t i n g w i t h t h e m a n a g e r s o f y o u r c o m p a n y t o t r a c k y o u r start-up's progress. E a c h m e e t i n g has the s i n g u l a r
purpose o f d e t e r m i n i n g i f y o u r p l a n is succeeding. Start by t a k i n g a l o o k at w h a t y o u expect t o h a p p e n and c o m p a r e i t t o
w h a t ' s a c t u a l l y h a p p e n i n g . T a l k a b o u t m e a s u r a b l e t h i n g s : are the n u m b e r s w h a t t h e p l a n expects t h e m t o be? S h o u l d y o u
adjust y o u r p l a n t o c o m p e n s a t e f o r a n y setbacks? W e r e t h o s e setbacks due t o a f l a w i n the p l a n o r t o u n r e l a t e d c o m p l i c a t i o n s ?
A d j u s t y o u r plans a c c o r d i n g l y .
M a k e sure t h a t a l l r e l e v a n t t e a m m e m b e r s are i n f o r m e d ahead o f t i m e w h e n these m e e t i n g s w i l l occur. K e e p t h e m short a n d t o
the point.
4.

Examine Your Execution

O n e o f the best reasons t o consider c h a n g i n g y o u r plans i n v o l v e s e x e c u t i o n . T h e best plans w o n ' t w o r k i f y o u can't execute
t h e m w e l l . Y o u m a y n o t be able t o p u l l i t o f f for m a n y reasons, f r o m l a c k o f c a p i t a l t o n o t h a v i n g the r i g h t people i n y o u r
t e a m . I f y o u r e x e c u t i o n f a i l e d , can y o u fix the cause o f the f a i l u r e ? C a n y o u a f f o r d t o h i r e t h e r i g h t people t o get y o u r
m a r k e t i n g c a m p a i g n o f f t h e g r o u n d ? C a n y o u get t h e capital t o e x p a n d y o u r o p e r a t i o n s ? I f there is n o feasible w a y t o m a k e
y o u r plans w o r k , g i v e n y o u r c o n t e x t , y o u m a y h a v e t o change y o u r plans.

JOINT VENTURE POWER! with Robin J. Elliott
A S i m p l e Question that could Revolutionize y o u r Business
I f I asked y o u i f you could double your sales in the next t w o
weeks, y o u w o u l d probably respond that it w o u l d impossible. I f
I asked y o u i f you could enroll ten people i n the next t w o weeks,
I'd probably get the same response. B u t i f I asked y o u a question
that w o u l d supercharge your level o f motivation from
acceptance and compliance to desperation and extreme
urgency...
W h a t i f you were absolutely convinced that y o u r family w o u l d
be viciously and brutally slaughtered i f you didn't double your
sales or enroll ten new people i n the next t w o weeks? That's the
question, folks. I f you believed that, what w o u l d y o u differently?
W h a t w o u l d y o u start doing that y o u have stopped doing? W h o
w o u l d y o u approach that y o u are presently intimidated by? H o w
w o u l d your approach and attitude change?
W h e n w e fear not achieving our goals more than w e fear the
opinions o f other people, everything changes. W h e n w e lose our
timidity and get serious and urgent enough to do whatever it
takes, w e can suddenly achieve massive results. W e w i l l
approach everyone w i t h o u t prejudging them. W e w i l l close more
effectively and more passionately, we w i l l be more focused, w e
w i l l follow up rigorously and diligently. W e w i l l zero o n what
we have to do and disregard distractions w h i l e overcoming
obstacles.
W h e n our dread o f "rejection" is dwarfed by our drive to
accomplish, w h e n our level o f motivation is white hot, w e
become an unstoppable force in sales and recruiting. In this
w o r l d o f the gutless "politically correct," w e are being
conditioned to overreact to the reactions and judgments o f
others. But w h e n y o u w e realize that nobody can "reject" Y O U ,
they can only decline A N O F F E R , and that they have every right
to do so, when y o u realize that those people don't care about
you, your family, your financial well-being, or your feelings, and
that y o u are doing them a F A V O U R by introducing them to your
product, service, or opportunity, y o u break free.
In order to succeed i n business, w e need to develop a thick skin,
we need to understand the numbers game o f ratios, and w e need
to get leverage o n our emotions. It is natural for people to to do
more to avoid a loss than to gain a benefit, so by imagining the
question posed about your family being slaughtered or another
horrific consequence o f not achieving your goal, y o u can start to
obtain an objective perspective o f what is truly possible and
important. Imagine i f your life was a dream and y o u k n e w y o u
were dreaming, w o u l d y o u be bolder?
The bottom line is this: Usually, the only thing currently
preventing us from doubling our sales and boosting our
recruiting is our fear o f the opinions o f others.
A burning desire is what w i l l take us to where w e want to be.
W h a t makes a relatively ill-equipped person excel against a l l
odds, w h i l e someone w h o has everything going for them fails
miserably? W h a t sets the real winners apart from the also rans?
W h i c h horse does one back? H o w can one predict w h o w i l l
succeed and w h o w i l l fail? A friend said, " W h e n your W H Y
makes y o u CRY, y o u can't help but succeed..."
It's not the economy, the past, slavery, competition, the products,
the marketing department, your upbringing, or Rodney i n

Receiving. It's not the tools or the
telephones or the leads or the
website. N o t even the training or the
compensation plan. O r your team.
Or your Team Leader. W h a t
determines your level o f success is
simply h o w badly y o u want it. A n d
without a burning desire that w i l l
not be denied or ignored, y o u w i l l
j o i n that sniveling, l u k e w a r m flock
who tried but failed. In the words o f
the great Les B r o w n , " Y o u gotta be
HUNGRY!"
In Dr. Hurd's excellent article, " D o n ' t Forget China," he writes,
"That's the real concern: N o t the number o f weapons a
government has; but the k i n d o f government w h o has them." I
agree. A determined, focused, highly motivated government w i l l
w i n , no matter what the odds. That's w h y V i e t n a m beat the
United States. A n d i f Vietnam could beat them, imagine what
China could do, especially w h e n enthusiastically w h e n backed
by Russia, Iran, and many others. T h e U S w o n ' t stand a chance.
The M u s l i m fundamentalists are calling the shots w o r l d w i d e as
w e l l ; right d o w n to controlling the pictures cartoonists draw and
Christian prayers in U S schools.
Is there any hint o f a question i n one's fertile imagination that
the alternately bowing and strutting, affirmative action
community organizer w h o sneaks around the W h i t e House
between his golfing bouts is any match for the head o f the K G B
trained Russian President?
B o t t o m line, those committed at the deepest level w i l l achieve
their objectives, regardless o f the tools and resources at their
disposal. Those w h o w i l l die for their cause w i l l definitely beat
those weaklings w h o are "politically correct" and afraid to
offend them. One can find and excuse or find a way.
" W h e n y o u discover y o u r m i s s i o n , y o u w i l l feel its
d e m a n d . I t w i l l fill y o u w i t h e n t h u s i a s m a n d a
b u r n i n g desire t o get t o w o r k o n it." ~ W . C l e m e n t
Stone
But then again, w h o am I to say? I live here in purportedly
unceasingly raining Vancouver, covered in moss, doing all I can
to avoid the pungent smoke o f the marijuana smoking tree
huggers and the hysterical screams o f the L G B T activists...

A u g u s t Smoggest... A Simple W a y To C u t
Through The Fog and Clear The P a t h To
Bigger Profits
H o p e y o u are h a v i n g a F A N T A S T I C s u m m e r so far!
T i m e flies fast a n d before w e k n o w it... C H R I S T M A S w i l l be h e r e ! W h i c h also m e a n s y o u r business a n d
personal goals m u s t be o n the r i g h t track by n o w , o r y o u need a serious reboot if y o u are going t o m a k e
it happen.
A b i g p a r t o f success i n m a r k e t i n g a n d b u s i n e s s is i n t h e s t o r i e s y o u tell y o u r p r o s p e c t s a n d clients. N o
b e t t e r w a y t o w i n s o m e b r o w n i e p o i n t s t h a n s h a r i n g s o m e p e r s o n a l t h i n g s g o i n g o n i n y o u r life. I've
tested using personal stories i n business to business A N D business to consumer - B O T H W O R K .
Actually B 2 B w o r k s even better because N O O N E does it! I did a campaign for a client a while back that
w a s targeted at the purchasing managers o f $ 1 0 0 m i l l i o n dollar type companies. B u s y guys. Lots o f
sales people t r y i n g t o w i n t h e m over.
W e didn't k n o w a soul. A cold list o f 2 0 0 o f these managers - s o m e o f t h e m even o w n e r s o f the company.
T h e letter I w r o t e talked about family, kids, dreams and aspirations. N O T H I N G like y o u r typical 'pitch'
letter o r brochure. Get this... 1 9 % o f t h e m responded to the letter! N o t just responded - but T H A N K E D
US for w r i t i n g such a personal letter. T r y t h a t w i t h a brochure!
Stories are y o u r secret w e a p o n i n 2 0 1 5 and beyond. USE T H E M . Here's one for you...
I h a v e k e p t c e r t a i n parts o f m y p e r s o n a l life p r e t t y q u i e t o v e r t h e past f e w years. R a r e for m e - b u t s o m e
major things happened that I wasn't comfortable sharing. W h y share t h e m n o w ? Because the past few
years taught m e a t o n o f p o w e r f u l things about i m p r o v i n g myself, and m y business...and I w o u l d like to
pass t h e m o n to y o u .
E a r l y January 2 0 1 2 , 1 w a s fed up. Fed up w i t h m e . Fed up w i t h m y health. Fed up w i t h the d i r e c t i o n m y
p e r s o n a l life w a s g o i n g . A n d fed u p w i t h c e r t a i n parts o f m y business.
Have y o u been there? W e all have. I did s o m e t h i n g about i t though. DRASTIC action. I ended up divorced
after 12 years o f marriage. T h a t w a s v e r y difficult - n o t s o m e t h i n g I w i s h o n anyone. B u t change w a s
n e e d e d . Fast f o r w a r d 3 y e a r s a n d e v e r y o n e is d o i n g fine, n e w l i v e s h a v e b e g u n , a n d p o s i t i v e c h a n g e s
c a m e as a r e s u l t . M O R E d r a s t i c change... m y h e a l t h .
I have always been active i n m a r t i a l arts and walking, b u t it wasn't enough. I carried far t o o m u c h extra
w e i g h t for the exercise I w a s getting, I didn't feel t h a t great, a n d I had lost m y self-confidence...
ultimately leading to depression.
So I did s o m e t h i n g a b o u t it. Fast f o r w a r d a f e w years a n d I dropped ~ 3 0 p o u n d s i n fat a n d p u t o n ~ 2 0
p o u n d s i n muscle. I feel great and m y self-confidence r e n e w e d .
M y business w a s a n o t h e r area I w a n t e d C H A N G E , massive change. Fast f o r w a r d a f e w years a n d I have
redesigned m u c h o f m y business and some M A S S I V E n e w developments are i n the w o r k s and thriving.

Want to double your sales "without" spending more time selling?
M y m a r k e t i n g a n d sales c o a c h i n g c l i e n t s a r e a l w a y s l o o k i n g f o r w a y s t o r a m p u p sales w i t h o u t r a m p i n g u p
t h e t i m e t h e y s p e n d selling. If y o u ' d like t o d o t h e s a m e , t h e n pull i n y o u r c h a i r a n d let's t a k e a close l o o k a t
o n e w a y t o achieve t h a t g o a l .
First, let's play w i t h s o m e n u m b e r s . Let's say y o u r average sale is $ 3 0 0 0 a n d let's say t h a t y o u m a k e o n e sale
per w e e k , based o n p r e s e n t i n g t h r e e q u o t e s a w e e k . In t h i s e x a m p l e y o u w o u l d h a v e a closing r a t i o o f 3 3 % ( o n e sale
for e v e r y t h r e e q u o t e s ) . If y o u m u l t i p l y $ 3 0 0 0 a w e e k t i m e s 5 2 w e e k s , it w o u l d m e a n y o u g e n e r a t e sales o f $ 1 5 0 , 0 0 0 a
year. (You m u s t h a v e a v e r y s m a l l business.)
Okay. N o w l o o k a t w h a t h a p p e n s w h e n y o u d o u b l e y o u r closing r a t i o , f r o m 3 3 % t o 6 6 % . N o w y o u still p r o d u c e o n l y
t h r e e q u o t e s a w e e k - m e a n i n g t h e r e is n o increase i n selling t i m e - b u t - a t a 6 6 % closing r a t i o t h i s m e a n s y o u m a k e
t w o sales each w e e k i n s t e a d o f o n e . T h a t m e a n s sales o f $ 6 0 0 0 p e r w e e k t i m e s 5 2 w e e k s f o r a n e w t o t a l o f $ 3 0 0 , 0 0 0
per year. ( H m m . N o w y o u r business i s n ' t so s m a l l ) .
How can you do it? With lots of magic, but no tricks ! Raising y o u r closing r a t i o is r e l a t i v e l y easy b u t it r e q u i r e s

close

a t t e n t i o n t o each o f a series o f e i g h t keys t o success:
The first key to success is to begin with the end in mind

As S t e p h e n C o v e y says i n his b o o k , " T h e 7 H a b i t s o f Highly Effective People," it's a l o t easier t o achieve y o u r g o a l i f y o u
begin by h a v i n g it clearly i n m i n d . S o m a k e u p y o u r m i n d - r i g h t a t t h e s t a r t - t h a t y o u w i l l close e v e r y sale t o q u a l i f i e d
prospects. ( W h e n y o u s h o o t f o r a h u n d r e d percent, 6 6 p e r c e n t l o o k s a l o t easier.)
The second key is relationship building.

M a k e sure t h a t y o u a n d e v e r y o n e y o u w o r k w i t h a n s w e r s e v e r y p h o n e call w i t h t h e i r first n a m e . W h e n a prospect calls
or visits, i n t r o d u c e y o u r s e l f ; ask f o r t h e i r n a m e ; w r i t e t h a t n a m e d o w n , a n d u s e i t o f t e n . S h o w g e n u i n e i n t e r e s t i n y o u r
prospect's n e e d s , w i s h e s a n d ideas i n r e l a t i o n t o y o u r p r o d u c t o r service (and listen f o r clues t o w h e r e t h e y h u r t i n a
w a y t h a t y o u c a n h e l p ) . Be " c o n v e r s a t i o n a l " instead o f " q u o t a t i o n a l , " as I like t o say. T h e key p o i n t h e r e is t h a t e v e n i f
t h e prospect is n o t a g o o d f i t f o r y o u , o r i s n ' t q u a l i f i e d t o buy, t h e y can still j o i n y o u r e v e r g r o w i n g a r m y o f "sales
a m b a s s a d o r s " - p e o p l e w h o h a v e d e a l t w i t h y o u ; fell i n love w i t h y o u ; a n d c a n ' t w a i t t o t a l k e n t h u s i a s t i c a l l y a b o u t y o u
to their friends.
The third key is qualifying

Q u a l i f y i n g m e a n s a s k i n g q u e s t i o n s w h i c h w i l l help y o u d e t e r m i n e if t h e prospect is "ready, w i l l i n g a n d able t o b u y n o w "
(and t o b u y f r o m y o u , as t h e y m a y be afraid o f l e a v i n g t h e i r p r e s e n t p r o v i d e r ) . Y o u h a v e t o ask y o u r q u a l i f y i n g q u e s t i o n s
in a d i s t i n c t l y h e l p f u l w a y - h e l p i n g t h e prospect g e t c l a r i t y o n t h e i r n e e d s , b u d g e t a n d t i m e f r a m e . If t h e y ' r e n o t
q u a l i f i e d . . . n o t ready, w i l l i n g a n d able t o b u y . . . t h e n offer t o keep t h e m i n f o r m e d w i t h y o u r n e w s l e t t e r a n d e m a i l
b u l l e t i n s (this is called "drip m a r k e t i n g " ) b u t d o n ' t consider t h e m a c a n d i d a t e f o r closing. W h e n asked f o r a price,
p r o v i d e a ballpark e s t i m a t e , a n d say y o u w i l l b e h a p p y t o p r o v i d e a m o r e d e t a i l e d q u o t e as t h e y g e t closer t o t h e i r t i m e
line, o r g e t t h e f u n d i n g t h e y n e e d , a n d so o n . If t h e i r budget
d o e s n ' t f i t f o r y o u r p r o d u c t o r service, t r y t o refer t h e m t o a
p r o v i d e r w h o w i l l be a great f i t f o r t h e m . D o n ' t w o r r y a b o u t
F o r m e r b u s i n e s s j o u r n a l i s t , N e i l G o d i n ( a . k . a . T h e T u r n a r o u n d Guy®) i s p u b lisher of "Marketing Dangerously," t h e world's only marketing a n d sales "idea
losing a sale. Focus o n c r e a t i n g a n o t h e r "sales ambassador."

service" for b u s i n e s s builders, a n d a u t h o r o f "Selling in t h e ( C o m f o r t )

The fourth key is to be perceived as a "trusted advisor"

W i t h o u t t a l k i n g d o w n t o y o u r prospect, m a k e it clear t h a t y o u a r e a n e x p e r t i n y o u r field. D o t h i s by asking h o w m u c h t h e y
k n o w a b o u t aspects o f t h e i r purchase...and o f f e r i n g t o clarify, e d i f y a n d e x p a n d t h e i r k n o w l e d g e . ( B T W Y o u can n e u t r a l i z e
sales resistance by saying t h i n g s like, " I f y o u ' r e c o m p a r i s o n s h o p p i n g , Pat, t h e r e a r e q u e s t i o n s y o u w i l l w a n t t o ask t o m a k e
sure y o u ' r e c o m p a r i n g a p p l e s t o apples. For e x a m p l e . . . " T h i s a c t u a l l y r e d u c e s t h e c h a n c e s o f t h e i r s h o p p i n g a r o u n d , b e c a u s e
y o u give y o u r s e l f a n o p p o r t u n i t y t o d e m o n s t r a t e y o u r e x p e r t i s e , a n d by so d o i n g , y o u m a y c r e a t e w e l l - f o u n d e d c o n c e r n i n
y o u r prospect a b o u t b u y i n g f r o m a n y o n e else.) A l s o , b e s u r e t o g a t h e r a n d share a n y t h i r d p a r t y e v i d e n c e t h a t s h o w s y o u can
be t r u s t e d . A n y m e d i a coverage y o u ' v e h a d . . . t e s t i m o n i a l s f r o m g r a t e f u l c u s t o m e r s . . . u n c o n d i t i o n a l g u a r a n t e e s . . . A + r a t i n g a t
t h e B e t t e r Business B u r e a u . . . a n y t h i n g t h a t relates t o y o u r p a r t i c u l a r t y p e o f business.
The fifth key is "Repeat and Referral Marketing"

W h e n y o u a r e selling t o a r e p e a t c u s t o m e r , closing y o u r sale is v i r t u a l l y c e r t a i n . S o . It is critical t h a t y o u stay in t o u c h w i t h
p r e s e n t a n d past c u s t o m e r s . M a k e a p o i n t o f n o t i n g o t h e r i t e m s o r services y o u c o u l d h a v e sold t h e m , a n d w h e n y o u call t o
check o n t h e i r s a t i s f a c t i o n (and d e a l w i t h a n y t h i n g t h a t m a y n e e d a t t e n t i o n ) , ask if t h e y w o u l d like a n e s t i m a t e ( o r j u s t ideas)
o n t h i s a d d i t i o n a l w o r k . In t e r m s o f r e f e r r a l sales, ask q u e s t i o n s like, "Pat, has a n y o n e s h o w n i n t e r e s t in t h e w o r k w e did w i t h
y o u ? " A n d . . . " w h o s h o u l d I b e t a l k i n g t o ? " A n d . . . " C o u l d I ask y o u t o i n t r o d u c e m e ( o r advise t h e m t h a t I'll be calling) so I can
a v o i d b o t h e r i n g t h e m w i t h a n u n s o l i c i t e d sales call?" C o n s i d e r o f f e r i n g i n c e n t i v e s like a " f a m i l y a n d f r i e n d s discount," o r a
" w h i l e w e ' r e i n y o u r n e i g h b o r h o o d " special offer. T h i n k h a r d a b o u t w a y s y o u can s t i m u l a t e r e f e r r a l business. A n d w h e n y o u
m a k e a r e f e r r a l sale, be s u r e t o say " t h a n k y o u " w i t h a special gift.
The sixth key is controlling communication with your prospect

O v e r a n d o v e r I h e a r t h e s a m e t a l e o f w o e . . . w h e n c l i e n t s say t h e y ' v e b e e n d u m p e d by a " p e r f e c t " prospect w h o is n o l o n g e r
r e t u r n i n g t h e i r calls. Tragically, t h i s h a p p e n s w h e n t h e y t h o u g h t a sale w a s a b s o l u t e l y c e r t a i n . W h y d o e s t h i s h a p p e n ? U s u a l l y
because t h e y p r e p a r e d a q u o t e o r p r o p o s a l ; sent it by e m a i l - t h e n f o l l o w e d up w i t h ( y o u guessed it), a " f o l l o w up call."
M a k i n g f o l l o w up calls is a n o r m a l , s t a n d a r d , e v e r y d a y p r o c e d u r e f o r business o w n e r s a n d sales p e o p l e - a n d it is a b s o l u t e l y
disastrous. W h y ? Because t o y o u , a f o l l o w up call is j u s t g o o d business - b u t t o y o u r prospect it m a y be a n a n n o y a n c e ( " w h y is
she b o t h e r i n g m e . . . l j u s t m e t w i t h h e r t w o days a g o ? " ) . Instead, stay i n c o n t r o l o f c o m m u n i c a t i o n . D o t h i s by n e v e r l e a v i n g
o n e m e e t i n g o r call w i t h o u t s e t t i n g up t h e date, t i m e a n d a g e n d a f o r t h e n e x t o n e .
The seventh key is avoiding sticker shock

M a n y a sale is lost - a n d a closing r a t i o is l o w e r e d - b e c a u s e t h e prospect suffers sticker s h o c k w h e n t h e y receive y o u r q u o t e .
S o l u t i o n : D o n ' t d o t h e n u m b e r s o n y o u r o w n . D o e v e r y t h i n g y o u can t o l e a r n w h a t t h e prospect h o p e s ( o r can afford) t o
s p e n d , w h i l e y o u are w i t h t h e m . T h i s can b e as s i m p l e as f l i p p i n g t h r o u g h iPad i m a g e s o f w o r k y o u ' v e d o n e f o r o t h e r s ; n o t i n g
t h e price range, a n d asking if t h a t price range is i n t h e i r ball park. T h e n , it is also i m p o r t a n t t h a t y o u p r e s e n t y o u r q u o t e o r
p r o p o s a l i n p e r s o n (live o r by t e l e p h o n e , Skype o r J o i n . m e ) , s o t h a t y o u can see a n d h e a r t h e i r r e a c t i o n a n d r e s p o n d
i m m e d i a t e l y t o a n y c o n c e r n s . If y o u s i m p l y e m a i l a n d t h e n m a k e a f o l l o w up call, y o u m a y literally b e s e t t i n g y o u r s e l f up t o get
dumped.
The eighth key is closing effectively

W h e n y o u r prospect is saying "yes" t o each e l e m e n t o f w h a t y o u ' r e p r o p o s i n g - because y o u l i s t e n e d h a r d , a n d m a d e sure
t h a t t h e i r needs, w i s h e s a n d h u r t s w e r e a d d r e s s e d - y o u can a s s u m e t h a t t h e y are ready t o buy. T h a t ' s t h e t i m e t o " a s s u m e
t h e close," a n d ask " h o w " t h e y w o u l d like t o m o v e f o r w a r d , n o t " i f " t h e y w a n t t o buy. For e x a m p l e , " I k n o w y o u like t h e g r e e n ,
Pat, b u t y o u ' v e l o o k e d back a t t h e red a n u m b e r o f t i m e s . . . w h i c h c o l o r are y o u g o i n g t o go w i t h ? " Or, "Okay, a design d e p o s i t
w i l l get t h i s i n t o t h e p r o d u c t i o n s c h e d u l e . . . w o u l d y o u like t o use a credit card, o r w o u l d y o u prefer t o use a c h e q u e ? " In m a n y
cases t h i s w i l l r e s u l t in a closed sale, h e r e a n d n o w . B u t t h e r e w i l l be t i m e s w h e n y o u r prospect w i l l i n t e r r u p t , saying t h e y ' r e
not s u r e a b o u t s o m e t h i n g . N o p r o b l e m . Take t h e q u e s t i o n s e r i o u s l y ; find a n acceptable s o l u t i o n , t h e n go back t o closing.
Special n o t e : If t h e y say, " W e ' l l h a v e t o t h i n k a b o u t it," offer t o h e l p . T h i n k back t o y o u r discussions. W a s t h e r e s o m e t h i n g
t h a t b o t h e r e d t h e m (budget, t i m i n g , scope o f t h e w o r k ) t h a t w a s n ' t fully r e s o l v e d ? A s k i f t h a t ' s t h e i r c o n c e r n , a n d d o all y o u
can t o r e s o l v e it n o w . If t h e y go o f f t o " t h i n k a b o u t i t " o n t h e i r o w n , y o u m a y n e v e r get t h e m back - a n d ( o f course) y o u r

FAST TRACK TO EBAY with Larry Yakiwczuk
e B a y a n d R e v e n u e C a n a d a ..
Today we are going to go a little off topic, well to be honest, a lot off topic.
We are going to talk about deals and the best time to get them. Everyone wants to get a deal and
save some money from retail pricing. That's why auctions are a wonderful tool to get good deals
at. You will generally be buying merchandise at a discount. However that is not the only way to
get deals. Sometimes you just have to keep your eyes open and actually see what you and
everyone else is looking at.
Also another way to generally find deals is to have a contrarian out look to things. When everyone is running in one direction,
it may make sense to go the other way. An example of this that most people have heard of is when there is a fire in a
crowded room. Everyone rushes for the one main door, and there have been cases where the sole survivors have made it out
because they went for the less obvious choice and went in another direction.
This is also very prevalent in the stock market. The real professionals are generally buying when everyone else is selling, or
they are selling when everyone else is buying. The single most important step to get a deal is to actually do something after
you get the information.
Procrastination and lack of action are the biggest killers of deals. Most people wait so long before they decide to do anything
that the opportunity has long disappeared by the time they actually act on it. When I am looking at sourcing products to sell
online, I generally need to make a decision within seconds of seeing the opportunity. Generally there is no right or wrong
decisions. It does not matter what you do, as long as you do something! Deciding not to do a deal is just as valid as deciding
to do that deal.
The real deal killer is the procrastination and indecision.
Real estate is a classic example that most people can relate to. Everyone knows that when the markets are down, that is the
time to buy, and when the markets are up its time to sell. BUT very few people actually do this. The current market in Alberta
is a prime example of this.
With oil prices at a record low level, the Alberta economy has the appearance of being in the tank. Whether that is true or
not, is arguable. However it is the perception that is important not the reality. (Personally I believe and think I can prove that
the economy is booming despite what everyone is saying) Everyone perceives the economy is bad, so they are not willing to
do anything. So as we have discussed, this is the perfect time to do something. Lots of properties are listed but not many are
selling. In my opinion this is the perfect time to look at acquisition of real estate in Alberta.
As an example I will give you a specific deal that I can across. There is a small main floor commercial condo in a residential
high rise in Edmonton. The price, if you can believe this, is only $99,999. It is probably the cheapest condo in Edmonton. It is
leased out and shows an 18% cash on cash return. Surprisingly nobody is interested in it. It has had very little exposure in the
market.
The only thing I can think of is that everyone thinks its not true
or that its to small to look at. I have to admit I am from the
second group. I think this would be a great deal for someone
starting out, since it is leased and there is no management to be
done with it. If anyone is interested in it, I am more than willing
to pass it on to them. Lets see how many of you readers have
the motivation to act and ask for more information.
At least this way I will get an indication if anyone is actually
reading my articles.

auctions, his f u l l - t i m e occupation ( a l o n g w i t h 2 employees
and a B I G w a r e - h o u s e ) . H e is also an active R e a l Estate

BALANCING ACT with Randall Orser
Entrepreneurship: 5 Things to Do Before Making
Someone Your Partner
O n e o f the t h i n g s y o u ' l l h a v e t o s t r o n g l y consider as a n entrepreneur is f i n d i n g a partner. A
partner can offer a l o t for y o u r start-up, f r o m a different skillset to a dissenting voice that
m a y lead t o better decisions. Y o u m a y n o t a l w a y s e n j o y h a v i n g to r u n t h i n g s t h r o u g h
another person, b u t the p o t e n t i a l benefits are t o o g o o d t o i g n o r e . T h e p r o b l e m is actually
b u i l d i n g a successful partnership. T h e r e are a couple o f t h i n g s y o u n e e d t o d o before c o m m i t t i n g t o a business
partner.
1. D o R e s e a r c h o n P o t e n t i a l P a r t n e r s
Y o u r partner's g o i n g to h a v e a l o t o f i n f l u e n c e a n d c o n t r o l o v e r y o u r start-up, so w h o y o u p i c k m u s t be t h o r o u g h l y
vetted and researched. People d o research o n w h e r e t h e y w a n t t o h a v e d i n n e r and that's j u s t a m e a l . Y o u s h o u l d d o
the same for potential partners.
T a k e a l o o k at t h e i r w o r k h i s t o r y . I s t h e r e a n y t h i n g t h a t c o n c e r n s y o u ? D o r e m e m b e r t h a t p e o p l e a r e f a l l i b l e a n d
w i l l m a k e mistakes. Focus o n the big picture. Study the context i n w h i c h they've succeeded or failed. W a s it
b e c a u s e t h e y w e r e t r y i n g s o m e t h i n g t h a t s e e m e d r e a s o n a b l e a n d p r o f i t a b l e at t h e t i m e o r d i d t h e y f a i l t o d o t h e
research? W a s their failure due t o a lack o f skill or because the tide turned at an inopportune t i m e ?
E x a m i n e t h e i r skillset. I d e a l l y , y o u ' l l h a v e as little o v e r l a p as possible w i t h y o u r partner. T h e y ' r e here t o p r o v i d e
diversity t h r o u g h their skills and connections, not do y o u r j o b .
2. Set G r o u n d R u l e s
A s a n entrepreneur, o n e o f y o u r j o b s is t o m a k e sure that e v e r y o n e i n the c o m p a n y k n o w s w h a t t h e i r roles are and
w h a t t h e y ' r e expected t o a c c o m p l i s h . T h a t goes f o r y o u r partner as w e l l . Y o u m u s t b o t h be clear o n w h a t y o u r
r e s p o n s i b i l i t i e s are. I f y o u can't r e a c h a n a g r e e m e n t o r f i n d i t d i f f i c u l t , it's t i m e t o l o o k f o r a n e w partner. It's h a r d t o
justify a partnership w h e n y o u don't sync w e l l w i t h t h e m .
3. F i g u r e O u t i f Y o u H a v e the S a m e V i s i o n
Y o u r partner w i l l h a v e t h e i r o w n reasons a n d goals, a n d that's o k a y . W h a t isn't o k a y is i f t h e y h a v e a c o m p l e t e l y
different idea o f h o w the start-up should be r u n and w h e r e to take it. Y o u m u s t agree o n w h a t k i n d o f c o m p a n y
c u l t u r e t o c u l t i v a t e , w h a t k i n d o f actions are acceptable a n d w h i c h o n e s aren't.
T a l k to y o u r potential partner and figure out i f y o u agree o n c o m p a n y culture and philosophy. Once y o u have that
i n f o r m a t i o n , observe h o w they treat people and h o w they live their lives. D o they have strong ties t o the
c o m m u n i t y ? D o t h e y h a v e l o n g - t e r m r e l a t i o n s h i p s ? D o t h e y l e a v e t h e i r w o r k at t h e o f f i c e o r a r e t h e y w i l l i n g t o
l e a p b a c k i n t o w o r k s h o u l d t h e c o m p a n y n e e d t h e m ? C o m p a r e w h a t y o u o b s e r v e t o w h a t t h e y t o l d y o u a n d see i f i t
fits w i t h w h a t y o u w a n t .

4. Start T h e m O f f o n a S i m p l e T a s k
Y o u don't w a n t t o leap into a partnership w h e n y o u don't k n o w h o w y o u r partner does things. S o g o f o r a trial r u n and
give t h e m something relatively simple to do. E x a m i n e h o w they d o things. D o they g o above and beyond what y o u
h a d t h e m d o ? A r e y o u h a p p y w i t h t h e q u a l i t y o f t h e i r w o r k ? D i d t h e y get it i n o n t i m e a n d i f t h e y didn't, d i d t h e y
make excuses?
5. B e P o l i t e i f It's N o t a G o o d F i t
T h e r e m a y c o m e a p o i n t w h e n y o u realize it's j u s t n o t a g o o d f i t . That's okay, there w i l l b e other candidates. T h e
p r o b l e m is h o w the split w i l l happen, as i t c a n happen before y o u o f f i c i a l l y b e c o m e partners o r late i n t o the
relationship. D o e v e r y t h i n g y o u can to m a k e sure that it goes s m o o t h l y . Y o u m a y be a n n o y e d o r e v e n frustrated w i t h
t h e d e v e l o p m e n t , b u t that's n o reason t o start b u r n i n g bridges. W h o k n o w s ? I n t h e f u t u r e y o u m a y r e q u i r e t h e i r help,
a l t h o u g h n o t as a partner.
I f y o u ' r e g o i n g t o get a partner, y o u m u s t m a k e sure that they're w o r t h t h e i r w e i g h t i n g o l d . Y o u ' r e a n entrepreneur
w i t h a start-up - there's a l o t a t stake. Just r e m e m b e r that a partnership takes t i m e t o d e v e l o p . T h e r e w i l l be g r o w t h
pains. I f y o u d o the research and don't settle f o r j u s t a n y o n e , y o u ' l l e n d u p w i t h a t e a m m a t e w h o ' l l c o v e r y o u r back
and help y o u raise y o u r start-up to the next level.

One day, as l o n g as y o u c o n t i n u e doing this, y o u w i l l get r e w a r d e d w i t h greater sales n u m b e r s . You w i l l finally convince
t h a t s t u b b o r n prospect t h a t has never b o u g h t to FINALLY give y o u a chance and b u y s o m e t h i n g y o u offer.
If y o u give up o n w r i t i n g , t h e y w i l l go a w a y t h i n k i n g y o u aren't i n business or interested i n t h e m for clients. T h e r e w a s a
study done t h a t s h o w e d 6 3 % o f people w h o left t o b u y f r o m a c o m p e t i t o r d i d so because t h e y t h o u g h t t h e o r i g i n a l
c o m p a n y d i d n ' t care a b o u t t h e m (ie. T h e y never heard f r o m t h e m since t h e y expressed i n t e r e s t o r b o u g h t ) .
M o s t companies o u t t h e r e don't e m a i l t h e i r clients and even i f t h e y do, t h e y e m a i l t h e m b o r i n g stuff t h a t doubles as
great i n s o m n i a cures. W h i c h explains w h y so m a n y businesses end up closing t h e i r doors... t h e y d o n ' t have e n o u g h
buyers, b u y i n g o n a regular basis.
Easily fixed w i t h regular and e n t e r t a i n i n g emails f r o m y o u to t h e m .

Fellow business builder,
T o m e , i n t e r n e t - o n l y m a r k e t i n g is m i s s i n g t h e boat. F o c u s i n g a l l o f y o u r m a r k e t i n g e f f o r t o n l i n e m a y be
d o i n g y o u m u c h m o r e h a r m t h a n g o o d . Yes - e m a i l is 'free'. Yes, w e b s i t e s a r e n e x t t o 'free'. A n d yes, y o u
can test m u c h faster and w i t h m o r e detail t h a n doing offline m a r k e t i n g .
B u t , w h e n I p e r s o n a l l y get 4 2 0 - 5 5 0 % b e t t e r r e s u l t s u s i n g p r i n t . . . m y r a d a r tells m e t h a t s o m e t h i n g is
amiss i n cyberworld.
I ' m talking about the l o w l y piece o f paper that people have to actually touch. T h a t t h i n g that wasn't
s u p p o s e d t o exist i n t h e 'paperless' office - H A ! I have m o r e p a p e r n o w t h a n ever before.
A n y h o w , for m y clients and prospects... I opt to n o t o n l y send t h e m e m a i l newsletters - but to also send
t h e m print newsletters.
Why?
• T h e y can't delete i n a n a n o second.
• T h e y have to physically handle it (even to t h r o w it out).
• T h e y can pass i t to others.
• T h e r e is M U C H m o r e p e r c e i v e d v a l u e i n p a p e r t h a n o n t h e screen.
• T h e r e is less c o m p e t i t i o n i n t h e p h y s i c a l m a i l b o x t h a n i n t h e e m a i l b o x ( I d o n ' t k n o w a b o u t y o u b u t I don't get 5 0 0 pieces o f stuff i n m y physical m a i l b o x to deal w i t h every day - I do i n m y i n b o x ) .
• T h e y are m u c h less likely to get upset w i t h y o u abusing t h e i r m a i l b o x t h a n t h e i r inbox.
And...
• T h e results speak for themselves!
W h e n I r u n a p r i n t n e w s l e t t e r I use different l i n k s I can t r a c k b a c k t o t h e specific source o f order. A n d
the n u m b e r s speak for themselves. F r o m a print ad I ran i n one newsletter, I saw a $ 8 . 6 1 p e r click
r e t u r n . F r o m the s a m e ad i n m y ezine I s a w a $ 0 . 7 6 p e r c l i c k r e t u r n .
W e l l o v e r 1 , 0 0 0 % better... s a m e ad... s a m e p r o d u c t . . . m a n y o f t h e s a m e contacts. B u t p r i n t c o n v e r t e d
e x p o n e n t i a l l y better.
I go w i t h w h a t w o r k s - and this w o r k s .
So, I t h o u g h t I w o u l d s h a r e w i t h y o u o n e o f m y n e w s l e t t e r s a n d h o w I s t r u c t u r e i t ( a n d h o w y o u s h o u l d
too).

Those stories they told are pure gold!

Here are some o f the parts I recommend y o u include in y o u r newsletter:

1) I n t r o d u c t o r y rant: a small section devoted t o what's o ny o u r m i n d this m o n t h . Your

2)

C a s e s t u d i e s a n d t e s t i m o n i a l s : y o u r t i m e t o s h o w o f f a n d s t r u t y o u r stuff. T h i s is y o u r
c h a n c e t o s h a r e y o u r clients w i t h y o u r p r o s p e c t s . T h i s is y o u r c h a n c e t o s h o w o f f h o w
g o o d y o u are. T h i s is y o u r c h a n c e t o m a k e y o u r clients d e v o t e d fans f o r life ( w h y w o u l d
t h e y go a n y w h e r e else w h e n t h e y get free p u b l i c i t y f r o m you?!)

3) F u n n y sayings, signs, b u m p e r stickers, o r s t r a n g e facts: everyone loves a good laugh
and a good read. Y o u r clients are n o different. Give t h e m s o m e good m a t e r i a l that makes
y o u r newsletter a M U S T read.
4)

Usable c o n t e n t a n d articles: Start w r i t i n g h o w to tips and stories about y o u r product or
service, it's h i s t o r y , h o w t o u s e i t better, a d v a n c e d tips... etc. I f y o u r e f u s e t o d o t h i s
y o u r s e l f , h i r e i t o u t ( w h i c h m a y n o t b e a w i s e m o v e as w r i t i n g is t h e B E S T m o v e y o u ' l l e v e r
m a k e as a b u s i n e s s o w n e r ) .

5) Calls t o a c t i o n a n d s o m e a d v e r t i s e m e n t s : the real key to m a k i n g y o u r newsletter
profitable. Don't over do it - b u t m a k e sure y o u do it! Consider it a M U S T to have at least 2
offers i n y o u r newsletter. One p r o v e n one - - a n d one n e w one y o u w a n t t o test.
Also note that y o u can get a 4 page newsletter p r i n t e d for D I R T C H E A R Y o u can even have other
people pay y o u to advertise i n y o u r newsletter - and have t h e m finance the entire thing.

Aim for 30% content and 70% other.
It m a y s o u n d s t r a n g e - b u t t h e f o r m u l a w o r k s .

Being Ready for The B i g Opportunity
It was N o v e m b e r 1973, a n dScot Halpin, a19year-old, scalped tickets t o T h e W h o concert i n
San Francisco. Keith M o o n , thedrummer, h a da
case o f the nerves. W h e n h e v o m i t e d before t h e
concert, h et o o k s o m e tranquilizers t o c a l m d o w n .
T h e drugs w o r k e d all too well. D u r i n g the show,
M o o n ' s d r u m m i n g became slow, then, halfway
through " W o n ' t Get Fooled Again," he slumped
onto his drums. M o o n was unconscious. W h i l e
the roadies tried t o bring h i m back t o form, T h e
W h o played as a trio. T h e d r u m m e r returned, b u t
only briefly and collapsed again, this t i m e
heading o f f to the hospital t o gethis stomach
pumped.
Scot H a l p i n w a s w a t c h i n g the action f r o m near
the stage. Y e a r s later, h e said, " m y f r i e n d got real
excited w h e n h e saw that M o o n w a s g o i n g t o pass
out again. H e started t e l l i n g the security guy, y o u
k n o w , this guy can help out. A n d all o f a sudden,
out o f n o w h e r e comes B i l l G r a h a m , " the great
concert promoter. G r a h a m asked H a l p i n straight
up, " C a n y o u d o it?," and H a l p i n shot back "yes."
W h e n Pete T o w n s h e n d asked the crowd, " C a n
anybody play t h e drums?" H a l p i n mounted the

confidently playing the blues j a m " S m o k e
Stacked L i g h t i n g "that soon segued into
"Spoonful." I twas a w a y o f testing the k i d out.

E y e . " B y t h e t i m e it was over, H a l p i n w a s
physically exhausted.

Townshend, John Entwistle a n dScot H a l p i n
t a k i n g a b o w center stage. T o t h a n k h i m f o r his
efforts, T h e W h o gave h i m a concert jacket.
A s t h e genius Ian A n d e r s o n w r o t e i n the lyricso f
Jethro Tull's " T h i c k as a B r i c k , " " I really don't
m i n d i f y o u sit this o n eo u t . . . " B u t here's m y

H a v e a n abundance outlook instead o f one o f

i n n o v a t o r s , t h e w i e r d o s . T h e y r u n east w h e n the

W h e n w e areabundance thinkers, w et h i n k about
w h a t is possible, w h y things w i l l w o r k , h o w w e

Scarcity thinkers t h i n k about the downside w h i l e
abundance thinkers t h i n k about the upside.
W h a t y o u t h i n k about comes about. T h e w a y w e
see o p p o r t u n i t y i s w h a t w e w i l l a c h i e v e . W e s e e

a l w a y s have a sense o f entitlement and expect t o
get " s o m e t h i n g f o r n o t h i n g , " o r t o g e tbailed out,

doesn't deserve i to r earn it.
A negative cynic is usually s oskeptical that
everything looks like a scam t o h i m , h e believes
everyone is trying t orip h i m off, and h e insults
one's integrity w i t h his inferences until o n e
avoids h i m . A loser loses because o f the w a y h e
thinks. J i m R o h n said w e should w o r k m o r e o n
ourselves than w e d o o n our businesses. Change
the lens, and everything changes.

and responsibilities, y o u r opportunities, and the

FAST TRACK TO EBAY with Larry Yakiwczuk
Realistic G o a l Setting

T h i s m o n t h w e are going t o talk about setting realistic goals a n d expectations. I n
m y experience o n e o f the biggest h i n d r a n c e t o a c h i e v i n g great success is t h e fact
that m o s t people set unrealistic goals that c a n never b e achieved. T h i s does
nothing more than kill your will to w o r k andy o u endup with nothing.
T h i s is especially true w i t h people starting o u t a n ebay sales business. T h e y get
all caught u p i nt h e h y p e f r o m these shameless U S ebay promoters w h o p r o m i s e
the m o o n w i t h none o f the w o r k .
A person gets sucked i n t o b u y i n g o n e o f their vastly overpriced courses w i t h t h e p r o m i s e that they w i l l
start e a r n i n g thousands o f dollars a m o n t h w i t h essentially n o w o r k because t h e y a r e g o i n g t o use a drop
shipping system. I have talked multiple times about the old drop shipping scam so I w o n ' t waste time
doing i t again.
I n s t e a d I w a n t t o t a l k a b o u t s e t t i n g y o u r g o a l s w h e n y o u first s t a r t . I f y o u a r e j u s t s t a r t i n g o u t s e l l i n g o n
ebay, d o n ' t expect t o b e m a k i n g thousands o f dollars a m o n t h . It's possible b u t n o t v e r y likely. Y o u n e e d t o
start s m a l l a n d w o r k y o u r w a y u p t o those dollar values. Instead o fsetting initial goals u s i n g d o l l a r values,
y o u a r e b e t t e r o f f s e t t i n g i n i t i a l s a l e s n u m b e r g o a l s s u c h a s w a n t i n g t o s e l l 1 0 i t e m s i n y o u r first m o n t h ,
t h e n 15 i t e m s i ny o u r second m o n t h , a n d so o n .

BALANCING ACT with Randall Orser
6 Warning Signs that Your Business is in Trouble

O w n i n g o r m a n a g i n g a s m a l l business is n o t for the faint o f heart. Business
o w n e r s w i l l b e able to tell y o u that there i sa m u l t i t u d e o f p r o b l e m s that need
to b e faced a n d r e s o l v e d e v e r y day. I t is n o t easy t o stay focused, c o m m i t t e d a n d m o t i v a t e d .
Successful entrepreneurs have the ability to spot signs o f trouble quickly, and to i m p l e m e n t
effective measures t o solve the problems. Fortunately, there are w a r n i n g signs that, i fheeded, can
help a business o w n e r or manager to address p r o b l e m areas that can potentially lead to the
downfall o f a business.
1. C a s h F l o w
O n e o f the earliest signs o f t r o u b l e i sa cash f l o w that is under pressure. W h e n there are n o t e n o u g h
funds available to pay salaries o r suppliers o n time, serious action i s required. Clear and concise
processes need to b ei n place to track the cash w i t h i n a business. I fy o u do not k n o w h o w m u c h
cash y o u spend and generate t h r o u g h y o u r business o n a d a i l y basis, y o u are a t risk.
2. P r o f i t
T h e m a i n r e a s o n w h y s o m e o n e starts a business i s t o generate a profit. I f y o u r business requires
additional f u n d i n g o n a regular basis, o r i fthe profit m a r g i n s are e x t r e m e l y l o w , y o u m a y need t o
r e c o n s i d e r y o u r b u s i n e s s m o d e l . I t i s c r u c i a l t h a t r e a l i s t i c l o n g a n d s h o r t t e r m t a r g e t s are set, a n d
that the actual p e r f o r m a n c e i sm e a s u r e d against the targets.
3. S e r v i c e o r P r o d u c t C o m p l a i n t s
I f y o u receive a h i g h v o l u m e o f complaints about the level o r service or quality o f y o u r products,
take note a n d act q u i c k l y . B u s i n e s s i sa l l a b o u t trust, service a n d quality. I f y o u i g n o r e serious
service o r p r o d u c t issues, y o u w i l l r u n o u t o f c u s t o m e r s s o o n e r rather t h a n later.
4. P o o r l y T r a i n e d S t a f f
T h e people that y o u e m p l o y i n y o u r business are y o u r b r a n d ambassadors. P o o r l y t r a i n e d staff, o r
staff that does not have the required skill level, w i l l bankrupt y o u r business. D o not e m p l o y people
that are incapable o f p e r f o r m i n g the r e q u i r e d tasks. Strict selection policies a n d a solid t r a i n i n g
p r o g r a m can help to sort out this issue.
5. F o c u s o n C o r e B u s i n e s s A c t i v i t i e s
Businesses that expand rapidly, or f o r m alliances w i t h other companies, can lose focus o n the core
activities o f the business. I fy o u w a n t to f o r m alliances w i t h other companies, ensure that t h e y are

TURNAROUND MARKETING with Neil Godin
This month: How to turn telephone inquiries into sales - Part #2
Most businesses receive telephone inquiry calls from prospective customers. If that includes you, then pull
up your chair and let's do a deeper dive into ways to turn inquiries into sales. Ready? Here we go.
First a reality check.
I estimate that "more" than 50% of potential sales are lost right here, right now, when handling telephone
inquiries. Of course I can't quantify the number, and every business is different, but if you want to do an acid
test for your business, all you have to do is record the number of inquiry calls you receive (by day, week,
month), and the number of sales that are made to these callers. Typically, that number is very low - and can
easily be doubled (that's why I estimate that 50% or more of potential sales may be lost in this process).
Next: A motivator
Think about the benefit of doubling your "telephone conversion ratio." For example, if you could double the
number of appointments you set with qualified prospects, you could double your sales - without spending a
dime.
Now the how-to's
Here is the step by step procedure my clients use to handle telephone inquiries.
S t e p t t l . G e t on y o u r c a l l e r ' s s i d e .
Many people I work with feel abused by callers. They complain that callers are cagey. They want to get pricing
information without divulging very much about themselves or their needs - meaning they're hard to qualify and are difficult to get appointments with. Does this square with your experience? Perfect.
Now let's turn it around. The idea is to "stop" thinking that callers are abusive. Instead, we need to accept the
truth that our callers are just like us. Like us, telephone shoppers aren't abusive, they are just wary. How do we
know that shoppers are wary? Because "we" are wary when we are shopping around. In fact, if you want to
know anything about shopper behavior, just think about how you behave, personally.
If you think of your caller as a person "who is just like you," you can easily relate to, and empathize with, their
wariness tactics. Now you can easily understand why they want to extract price information from you, without
giving too much away. The key to your success is empathy - meaning the willingness, and the ability, to see the
situation from the other person's point of view. If you decide to empathize, and really work on your
communication skills when handling inquiry calls, you are well on your way to increasing your conversion ratio.
Because now you can be on the caller's side.
S t e p # 2 . Use a t e l e p h o n e i n q u i r y checklist

(and log every

call)

Develop a telephone inquiry checklist (columns are usually
headed with "Caller's name?" "Introductions?" (did you get
on a first names basis?); "Needs analysis?" (qualifying
questions); "Appointment made?" "Telephone and email
contact information?" "How they heard about you?" "Followthrough notes," and so on). Your checklist acts as a prompt,
reminding you of the qualifying questions you need to ask,
and reminding you that your goal is to set an appointment if
the caller is qualified.
S t e p # 3 . Take

control of the conversation

Most sales opportunities are lost right from the start, because
we fail to take control of the conversation with callers. For
example, if I say, "Good morning, ExWhyZee Company,
