T h e R o y a l B a n k , Telus, D u n & Bradstreet, S u b w a y and M c D o n a l d s , but
works mainly with smaller independ- ent businesses - and he specializes in
t u r n a r o u n d m a r k e t i n g w o r k w i t h s m a l l t o m i d - s i z e c o m p a n i e s in c r i s i s . I n
these turnaround cases, sales a l w a y s h a v e to be doubled or tripled—
i m m e d i a t e l y — a n d a t m i n i m a l c o s t . In h i s s p e a k i n g , w r i t i n g a n d c o a c h i n g
work, Neil shares these turnaround ideas with o w n e r s of healthy businesses
w h o j u s t w a n t t o r a m p u p t h e i r s a l e s . If t h i s d e s c r i b e s y o u , t h e n N e i l
w e l c o m e s y o u r call or e m a i l . His strategies c a n help y o u i n c r e a s e y o u r s a l e s
- rapidly - n o matter w h a t business you're in, or w h a t condition y o u r
b u s i n e s s ( o r t h e e c o n o m y ) is i n . Y o u c a n r e a c h N e i l a t 1 . 8 0 0 . 5 6 3 . I D E A
(4332), or at n g @ n e i l g o d i n . c o m .

TURNAROUND MARKETING with Neil Godin
CONT'D
Neil here" I have just given up control of the conversation. This is so, because whoever asks the questions,
controls the call. In this case, I am inviting the caller to ask the questions (questions such as "could you tell
me the cost of AyBeeCee?"). Here is an example of a better opening:
"Good morning, ExWhyZee Company, my name is Neil, how can I help you this morning?"
Now that you have asked the opening question, it's easy to continue asking questions, as you move through the
"discovery" part of your call - where you try to learn as much as you can about the caller, and their needs, and
their readiness to buy. (By the way, when I say that you want to take control of the conversation, I don't mean
manipulating or taking control of the caller. They can, and will, do whatever they want - what you are doing is
taking control of yourself - as you manage the way you conduct these calls.)
Step #4. H a n d l e price questions strategically
Most of my clients are asked "product and price" questions at the beginning of telephone inquiry calls questions such as, "Can you give me a price on product or service 'X' please?" This brings up a great discussion.
Many people believe strongly that we should "never give out prices on the phone," while many others believe
that refusing to provide a price simply drives prospects away. I believe in a different approach. I believe we
should provide pricing (or better yet, a price range) but only if we are able to ask qualifying questions first. Here
is an example:

"Yes, I'll be happy to give you a ball park, Chris...but every job we do is customized, so I don't have a
price list to work from. I have two questions about your project that will tell me what I need to know in
order to give you a decent estimate. First..."
"Chris, your cost on this can vary by hundreds of dollars, depending on the options you choose...but I
have a couple of questions that will help us nail down your price range - and I may also be able to give
you some ideas on how you can save money. First, I need to know..."
Your questions will help you qualify the prospect's real needs (the hurt they want to heal or the wish they want
to fulfill), while helping the caller get a better understanding of what they really need as well. This approach
also begins to place you in the coveted position of a "trusted advisor," instead of a typical salesperson. This is
critical to your success.
Key points:
Offering product and price information without qualifying - and without making every effort to get an
appointment if the caller is qualified - is like making a donation to competitors, as your price may
simply be used for comparison shopping, as your caller attempts to find a better deal elsewhere.
If may seem that your caller simply "wants" a price. But what they actually "need" is a solution to their
problem, at a price they can afford.
If your caller asks you to email information, use the same approach (e.g. "Yes, Chris, I'll be happy to
email you an information package...now to be sure I include the right information, I need to ask you..."
After asking questions that help you understand the caller's real need, provide a budget range, rather
than a fixed price, if possible.
Note that in these examples we are not asking permission to ask the caller questions; instead we're
being assertive...we are stating that we need more information, and we're simply going ahead and
asking our questions. This approach helps you maintain control of the conversation, and helps you
establish your role as trusted advisor.

TURNAROUND MARKETING with Neil Godin - CONT'D
S t e p # 5 . Ask q u a l i f y i n g q u e s t i o n s in a h e l p f u l w a y
Make a list of qualifying questions that you refer to every time you handle an inquiry. Key questions usually include:
Timing - when they plan to purchase, install, occupy etc
Budget - what they expect, or hope, to spend
Scope - how much work or product they plan or need to purchase
Decision maker(s) - are you speaking to the person(s) who will decide?
Motivation - Are they experiencing a strong pain or desire that your product/service would address?
Other? - Anything else you need to know?
As you know, many callers are reluctant to disclose their budget. Like you and I, they fear that once you "have their number,"
you may manipulate things to ensure your price takes up the full amount. So, we need to find subtle (and helpful) ways to
learn their price range. One way to elicit budget information is to talk about other projects you've done that are similar to
what your caller is describing, and stating the price range of each example (e.g. "Chris we just did a project similar to yours on
the west side. They needed a little more area covered than you, but their project was pretty similar and was in the $2500 to
$3000 price range. Is that roughly the budget range you're thinking of?"
Key point: I think it's imperative that you determine the caller's hopes or expectations around price range before you leave the
call - and before you do any work, such as preparing an actual quote, or doing product/service research, and so on.
Otherwise you may encounter "sticker shock" that can kill the sale - and make all your work a waste of time. (When prospects
experience sticker shock, they react by no longer returning calls or emails. After being dumped by enough of these prospects,
we may come to believe that callers are out to abuse us, when the abuse we're suffering is actually self inflicted. Remember,
your callers behave the same way you do. The solution is to prevent sticker shock from happening in the first place.)
Key point: If appropriate in your business, ask the caller if they are at or near a computer, or have wifi, and invite them to visit
a web page that shows examples of your work - so they can see projects that are similar to theirs, while you describe the
work that was done and the price range. This kind of engagement raises the likelihood of a sale dramatically - while helping
you better understand their needs and wants - and their expectations around price.
S t e p # 6 . Suggest

a n a p p o i n t m e n t if t h e c a l l e r is q u a l i f i e d

If your prospect is qualified, offer to help them by meeting in person - either by inviting them to come to your business (if
appropriate) or offering to come to them - where you can meet each other "live and in person;" see first hand what they are
dealing with, and how you could help with practical advice.
Key point: The idea is to present a live appointment as an "opportunity" for the caller. Here's an example of this approach,
where a kitchen renovation salesperson suggests a meeting at the prospect's home:
"Chris it sounds like you're serious about moving ahead, so I'd be happy to come out and give you a complimentary
design consultation. Let's set up a time when I can come out and look at your ideas; measure up your space - and
walk you through our 3D design software. It will show you and Adele what your ideas will actually look like, and lets
you move things around. You also may find that there are things we can do to get you and Adele the look and
features you want, while saving you money. We don't charge for this service, and there's no obligation - and if you're
still shopping around you'll have a much better idea of what to look for and ask about. I'm going to be in your
neighborhood on Monday and Wednesday evenings next week. Would either work for you?"
Key point: If you can qualify a caller, and get an appointment during this first contact, your chance of closing - of converting
the telephone inquiry into a sale - rises dramatically. So, it's worth spending a "lot" of time thinking about how to qualify in
ways that are comfortable both for you and the caller - and how to word your offer to meet with them personally. Over to
you - and see you next month.

Serial killers b e h a v e like b e e s . T h e y c o m m i t their c r i m e s close t o h o m e , but far a w a y e n o u g h t h a t t h e
neighbors don't get suspicious. Similarly, bees collect pollen near their hive, but far e n o u g h that predators
can't find t h e hive. T o u n d e r s t a n d h o w this "buffer z o n e " w o r k s , scientists s t u d i e d b e e b e h a v i o r a n d w r o t e
up a f e w a l g o r i t h m s . T h e i r findings i m p r o v e d c o m p u t e r m o d e l s police u s e to find felons.

JOINT VENTURE POWER! with Robin J. Elliott
B o l t i n g o n Blinders? Here's m y Promise to Y o u
One o f the most dangerous things that True Believers do i n
business is when they start bolting on blinders. They are setting
themselves up for failure and ensuring that any recovery w i l l be a
long, hard road.
Anyone w h o has read Eric Hoffer's "The True Believer" w i l l
recognize that these cult members don't start off as fanatics, but
gradually become so. A n d to the extent that they lock their minds
out o f any other business possibilities or alternatives, they bolt on
those figurative blinders. Recovery from any cult is fraught with
agonizing adjustments, like a drug addict going through cold
turkey, and the business true believer is not immune.
I remember talking w i t h an acquaintance w h o was a failing
insurance salesmen (that was before they stuck the ridiculous label
o f "Financial Planner" on their greasy foreheads.) I n spite o f the
fact that he acknowledged that he was slipping down into
bankruptcy, he adamantly refused to consider an alternative
"occupation," let along any other business opportunity. He "loved"
his "calling" too much, he told me.
True Believers refuse to see anything wrong in their business, even
when it is staring them in the face and hitting them over the head
w i t h a heavy saucepan. They refuse to criticize because they no
longer enjoy critical or objective thinking. Blind loyalty is further
fueled by unhealthy group dynamics.
True Believers refuse to accept that nothing in business lasts
forever. After 28 years in business, I have witnessed too many
organizations change, close down, reinvent themselves, get sold,
go bankrupt, change their compensation plans, fire their top
people, lay others off, turn into Ponzi schemes, and disappear to
believe that any o f them w i l l last forever, but a true believer
simply w o n ' t accept that.
And so he or she w i l l bolt on the blinders - invest everything,
refuse Plans B or C, risk everything, and even when the fire
engines and police and bankruptcy trustees are at the door, they
keep on believing, hoping, making excuses, overlooking, and
investing.
M y message? Wake up. Plans B and C are essential. Y o u don't
have to be distracted, but y o u regularly need to take a long, hard
look at the business you're involved w i t h , preferably with the help
o f an intelligent, experienced outsider. Check your lifeboats and
fix the fire escape. Maintain relationships outside o f your current
business; don't burn the wrong bridges. Reduce risk. Remain
mentally flexible and open minded. That way, y o u w i l l survive to
fight another day.
The only constant in life is change. Embrace it.

I promise y o u that our minds w o r k i n
the same way; i f we allow people to
dump bad thoughts and smelly ideas
and negative expectations in our
minds, and instead o f throwing it out,
we w a l l o w around in it like pigs, our
businesses w i l l fall to pieces. W e w i l l
attract pretenders and losers like rats
and cockroaches, w e w i l l lose our
best team members, and our incomes
w i l l disappear like the real value o f
the U S dollar.
The best w a y to make sure we rise to the top i n business is to fill
our minds w i t h upbuilding ideas, great expectations, solid
information, and positive plans. This w e can easily accomplish by
reading the right books, associating w i t h the right people, and
learning from the best mentors.
I drilled Paul J. Meyer's M i l l i o n Dollar Personal Success Plan into
my heart and mind using spaced repetition when I started i n m y
own business 28 years ago, and I P R O M I S E Y O U that y o u cannot
fail by living according to it and building your business in this
way:
1. Crystallize Your Thinking. Determine what specific goal y o u
want to achieve. Then dedicate yourself to its attainment w i t h
unswerving singleness o f purpose, the trenchant zeal o f a crusader.
2. Develop a plan for achieving your goal, and a deadline for its
attainment. Plan your progress carefully: hour by hour, day by day,
month by month. Organized activity and enthusiasm are the
wellsprings o f your power.
3. Develop a sincere desire for the things y o u want i n life. A
burning desire is the greatest motivator o f every human action.
The desire for success implants "success consciousness," w h i c h i n
turn creates a vigorous and ever-increasing "habit o f success."
4. Develop supreme confidence i n yourself and your o w n abilities.
Enter every activity without giving mental recognition to the
possibility o f defeat. Concentrate on your strengths, instead o f
your weaknesses. Focus on your powers, instead o f your problems.
5. Develop a dogged determination to follow through on your
plan, regardless o f obstacles, criticism or circumstances or what
other people say, think or do. Opportunities never come to those
who wait; they are captured by those w h o dare to attack.
Ask me about three excellent options y o u may not yet have
considered. Robin Elliot

Here's m y promise to you:
I promise y o u that, i f you allow people to dump all their rooting
garbage in your living room, pretty soon it's going to stink to high
heaven, and decent people w i l l avoid your home like the plague.
Your family w i l l leave. The price o f your home w i l l plummet
through the smelly floor, and rats and cockroaches w i l l invade
your living space.

FAST TRACK TO EBAY with Larry Yakiwczuk
M o v i n g from offline...to online...to offline
Most businesses start with a brick and mortar type store and then after some time they decide
to try and take their businesses online. Inevitably most of those businesses run into trouble and
either fail or just close out their online presence because it starts to drag them down. The main
reason they run into problems is that they do not realize that the methods they use in a
conventional store generally do not work online. However it is quite easy to take your online
marketing and apply it to a conventional store or business. So why not do things backwards to
what most people do? Start a small online sales business and then once you have that figured out, take it offline and open
up a traditional store front. Then grow both businesses at the same time, giving you two different income streams.
Of course I advocate that everyone should have their own ebay sales business. It is the perfect small business to generate
some income from online sales. It also gives you the opportunity to expand it at your own pace and make it as big or small
as you want. Generate an extra few dollars a month to a few thousand dollars a month, the choice is yours. In the past the
biggest complaint from beginning sellers, is that they cannot source product to sell. In the past I have dedicated a number of
articles on how to source items for sale online. In the past I have also stated that I think the best source of items is to simply
do consignment sales. With this method you not only get items to sell, but you don't even have to tie up your own cash into
inventory. People still complain that they still cannot get items to sell online. Well I am here to tell you that not only can you
get enough items to sell online but in fact you will end up getting too much to sell. And when that happens, that is the time
to think about opening a physical store to get rid of the excess inventory, and the inventory that is too big or not appropriate
to sell online. This is not only a good idea in theory but it also works in real life, and I have the proof to tell you.
Many of you are aware of Dave's Diamond and Peak Performers programs. These are great programs that can give
absolutely phenomenal results, and I want to tell you a story about one couple who was part of that program and did
exactly what I have mentioned above. Some time ago Jon and Andrea Stachyruk participated in Dave's programs and
Fasttrack. I Met them and mentored them over the past three years. They were selling on ebay and I helped them grow
their online business. They started doing consignment selling and quickly became one of the largest ebay consignment
sellers in Canada. Their consignment business has grown so much that they have far too much merchandise to just sell
online. This month was a very special one for them, as they have just their third anniversary of opening up a retail store
front to liquidate much of their excess inventory and start up another cashflow stream. Their outlet is approximately 2500
square feet and filled with over 20,000 different items. They are now called C2C Cards 2 Collectibles and are located at
10375-59 ave, in Edmonton Alberta. They have chosen to have limited operating hours on Friday-Saturday and Sunday from
11:00am to 5:00pm. If you are ever in the area I would strongly suggest you stop by and take a look at what exactly is
possible if you take action and actually do something. In less than 2 years, Jon went from having a dead end job, to being
the largest ebay consignment seller in Canada, and also opening a large retail sales outlet. He has gone from "working for
the man" to becoming the man!
I still work very closely with Jon and I know he is always looking for energetic people willing to learn and who can help him
out in the store or with his online sales business. If you are
interested in learning some of the real inside secrets to being
an online sales wizard, and willing to help Jon out with some
labor, I would strongly suggest you get in contact with him
directly and volunteer your services. Jon can be contacted
through email at info(5)crap2cash.com or email me and I can
give your info to Jon directly. So if you are in the Edmonton
area, take some action, contact us, and you also may see
dramatic changes in your life.

L a r r y Y a k i w c z u k is t h e f o u n d e r o f B u c k a r u E-bay
auctions, his f u l l - t i m e o c c u p a t i o n ( a l o n g w i t h 2 employees
and a B I G w a r e - h o u s e ) . H e is also an active R e a l Estate
investor and derivatives t r a d e r as w e l l . T o f i n d o u t m o r e
about L a r r y a n d his e-bay busi- ness, please visit his
website w w w . b u c k a r u . c o m . Y o u can e - m a i l L a r r y at

BALANCING ACT with Randall Orser
5 Management Mistakes That Are Hurting Your Profits

M a n a g i n g y o u r e m p l o y e e s c a n be a t r i c k y p r o c e s s . I t c a n b e d i f f i c u l t t o f i n d e m p l o y e e s w h o m
y o u t r u s t w i t h y o u r v i s i o n a n d y o u r b u s i n e s s . O n t h e o t h e r h a n d , i f y o u r b u s i n e s s isn't c u r r e n t l y
p e r f o r m i n g o n par w i t h y o u r e x p e c t a t i o n s , it's p o s s i b l e t h a t y o u r m a n a g e m e n t s t y l e is a t f a u l t .
L e t ' s t a k e a l o o k at s o m e t h i n g s y o u as a m a n a g e r m i g h t be d o i n g t h a t are j e o p a r d i z i n g t h e success o f y o u r c o m p a n y .
1.

You're too paranoid.

S u r e , y o u h a v e t o m a k e s u r e t h a t y o u r e m p l o y e e s are d o i n g w h a t y o u n e e d t h e m t o , b u t y o u s h o u l d n ' t g o o v e r b o a r d . I f
y o u are i n v e s t i n g m o r e t i m e a n d m o n e y i n t o m o n i t o r i n g y o u r e m p l o y e e s t h a n y o u are i n t o a c t u a l l y p r o d u c t i v e w o r k , y o u
n e e d t o stop. D o n ' t h o v e r a r o u n d y o u r e m p l o y e e s ' d e s k s c o n s t a n t l y t o k e e p a w a t c h o n t h e m . Y o u n e e d t o t r u s t t h a t t h e
p e o p l e y o u ' v e h i r e d are c a p a b l e o f p e r f o r m i n g t h e i r j o b s w i t h m i n i m a l s u p e r v i s i o n . A s l o n g as y o u ' r e c l e a r a b o u t w h a t
you need t h e m to do and have a regular feedback channel, let t h e m breathe a little.
2.

Y o u t h i n k o f y o u r s e l f as a f r i e n d t o y o u r e m p l o y e e s .

Y o u n e e d t o h a v e c o r d i a l r e l a t i o n s w i t h y o u r t e a m . A stressful w o r k e n v i r o n m e n t h a m p e r s p r o d u c t i v i t y . A t t h e s a m e
t i m e , y o u r employees need t o understand y o u r a u t h o r i t y and trust y o u to m a k e t o u g h decisions. I f y o u t r y t o o hard to b e
a part o f t h e g a n g , y o u ' l l l o s e t h e i r respect.
3.

Y o u t r y t o o h a r d t o m a k e y o u r office a ' c o o l ' place.

I f y o u ' r e c o n s t a n t l y t h i n k i n g a b o u t h o w y o u can add n e w r e c r e a t i o n z o n e s , l o u n g e areas a n d p e r k s f o r y o u r e m p l o y e e s ,
you're w a s t i n g y o u r t i m e . I f y o u w a n t to m a k e y o u r w o r k e n v i r o n m e n t m o r e i n f o r m a l , open up additional channels o f
c o m m u n i c a t i o n . M a k i n g sure y o u r e m p l o y e e s are e a s i l y a n d f r e e l y able t o c o m m u n i c a t e w i t h y o u a n d t h e i r c o l l e a g u e s
w i l l help y o u r business m o r e than an extra P i n g - P o n g table.
4.

Y o u w i t h h o l d feedback for the annual appraisal meeting.

I f y o u r e m p l o y e e s are d o i n g w e l l o r p o o r l y , t h e y n e e d t o k n o w a b o u t i t n o w , n o t s i x m o n t h s d o w n t h e l i n e . C o n s i s t e n t
feedback w i l l keep y o u r employees m o t i v a t e d and give t h e m the i n f o r m a t i o n they need to i m p r o v e their skillsets.
A d d i t i o n a l l y , w h e n y o u offer feedback to y o u r employees, don't m a k e it a comparison. Instead, focus o n their o w n skills
a n d h o w t h e y c a n get better at d o i n g w h a t t h e c o m p a n y n e e d s t h e m t o d o .
5.

Y o u avoid conflict.

R u n n i n g a business means that you're going to have to m a k e decisions that w i l l m a k e some people unhappy. T h e r e is
s i m p l y n o g e t t i n g a r o u n d t h i s aspect o f m a n a g e m e n t . W h e t h e r y o u ' r e t a k i n g a c t i o n b a s e d u p o n c e r t a i n m a r k e t - b a s e d o r
i n d i v i d u a l p e r f o r m a n c e f a c t o r s , y o u ' l l h a v e s i t u a t i o n s w h e n p e o p l e are u p s e t . I n s t e a d o f a v o i d i n g t h e s e s i t u a t i o n s ,
e m b r a c e t h e m as a n o p p o r t u n i t y t o i n t e r a c t w i t h y o u r e m p l o y e e s a n d use t h e i r v i e w p o i n t s t o i m p r o v e y o u r b u s i n e s s .
C r e a t i n g t h e o p t i m a l w o r k e n v i r o n m e n t is o n e o f t h e best t h i n g s y o u can d o f o r y o u r c o m p a n y . I f t h a t m e a n s c h a n g i n g
t h e w a y y o u m a n a g e p e o p l e , so b e i t .
U s e t h e g u i d e l i n e s a b o v e t o i m p r o v e t h e w a y y o u lead y o u r e m p l o y e e s so t h a t y o u r b u s i n e s s c a n b e n e f i t a s a r e s u l t .

November, 2015

$49.95

a Drunken Duck + a Bar Room Dog Fight
= a HELL of a Good Email Idea
- b yT r o y

W h i t e

One of my favourite sources of good story ideas is in the online news media. There is a GOLDMINE of
ideas out there for those paying attention. Just saw this one today, and thought it was the PERFECT
example of how you can use a news item and turn it into a promotion.
The story is at www.storyplaybook.com/duck The headline from the news article: Duck Wearing
Bow-Tie Walks Into Pub, Drinks Pint, Fights Dog, Loses
Wee bit tabloid style - but fascinating subject line! You may mock this - but there isn't an industry out
there that couldn't get readers, and buyers, using more of this type of story. The article goes on about a
guy who has a pet duck, and a pet dog. He takes both to a bar and feeds them a beer - go figure, a fight
breaks out and the duck gets hurt. The lessons are varied on how you can tie this in.
Here's a few for some of the industries represented within the Playbook readers:
* You got their attention through the story line
* Now build it into some business lessons...
* How to get attention in cluttered marketplace (or selling marketing services or consulting
services)
* Stay classy at all times (talking about the tie-wearing duck - great for affluent services,
opticians, jewelry, interior designers)
* Dangers of drinking too much (fitness people, health care, nutritional advice)
* Looking classy doesn't need to cost you a fortune (consignment stores)
* Tie it all back to a quick offer you can make.
Very simple formulas - that consistently work!

MY FAVOURITE NEWS SOURCES
Some of the places I personally use and love for story ideas are:
* Huffington Post (www.huffingtonpost.com)
* The Mirror (www.mirror.co.uk)
* Google (news.google.com)

Page 1

TURNAROUND MARKETING with Neil Godin
This month: Smart People Set S.M.A.R.T. Goals
I've just spent a great week working with a great client - STOR-X* Organizing Systems (HQ'd here in Richmond, BC) - on
planning and goal setting. STOR-X* is a fast growing professional closet and space design and manufacturing company,
with eleven franchises across Western Canada - and many more on the way (coming soon to a town near you?). I'm
helping them with several facets of business development, including supporting franchisees in setting sales goals for the
coming year. In thinking about what would be helpful to them, I also thought about what may be helpful to you - so - this
month let's look at goal setting. Obviously, developing demanding but realistic goals is critical to your success, but the key is to
establish S.M.A.R.T. goals that "set you up to succeed." Yes, I know. You already know about S.M.A.R.T. goals - but - are you
setting them? And are you following through? Let's take a quick look at how S.M.A.R.T. goals work.
What is a S.M.A.R.T. goal?
A S.M.A.R.T. goal is Specific, Measurable, Achievable, Results-oriented, and Time-lined. In writing your S.M.A.R.T. goals use
verbs - action words - to describe what you are going to do to achieve them. Here is a brief description of each of the
S.M.A.R.T. goal criteria.
S = Specific:
Avoid setting goals that are vague or very general or broad in their focus.
Instead, be specific. Instead of saying your goal is to increase sales by 20%, spell out "how" you plan to increase sales
by 20%. Identify each customer segment you deal with, and estimate and "choose" opportunities for growth in each
one.
In addition to thinking about growth in sales to customer segments, you may want to explore opportunities for growth
among your various product lines and services. Again, be specific.
You may also want to explore opportunities in terms of marketing and sales activities. If you plan to join a networking
group, state which group and by when. If you plan to start a daily sales networking program, state when and who you
will target (If you need tips on this idea, drop me an email). To hold your feet to the Are, consider buying a white board
annual calendar - and posting every marketing and sales activity that you plan in the coming year - and update it
continuously. This will help tremendously with your follow-through.
You may have opportunities to increase sales by focusing on skill building. For example, you may see an opportunity to
increase telephone inquiry conversions. If so, establish a baseline or benchmark in terms of your present conversion
ratio; note the skills you and/or your team members will need to hone that will increase your ratio (Building instant
rapport? Qualifying in more helpful ways? Focusing on the interests of your caller more than on what you offer?)
Also state "why" you plan to pursue each strategy - then go on to describe "how" you plan to execute your strategy
and achieve your goal.
By spelling out the "what," "why," "who," "when" and "how" of your goals, you "set yourself up to succeed" in setting
S.M.A.R.T. goals, and in actually achieving the goals you set.
Here is a little exercise to get you started. Exercise: Goal #1. (Write out the goal next to "What" then answer the other four
questions):
What?
Why?
How?
Who?
When?
Here is an example..

Former business journalist, Neil Godin (a.k.a. The Turnaround Guy®) is publisher of "Marketing Dangerously," the world's only marketing and sales "idea
service'' for business builders, and author of "Selling in the (Comfort)
Zone" (available at Amazon and other outlets). As a speaker Neil has
presented to more than 300,000 business people from coast to coast in
Canada and the United States. As a marketing and sales consultant and
coach, he has worked with many major companies, including Shell, Ford,
The Royal Bank, Telus, Dun & Bradstreet, Subway and McDonalds, but
works mainly with smaller tndepend- ent businesses - and he specializes in
turnaround marketing work with small to mid-size companies in crisis. In
these turnaround cases, sales always have to be doubled or tripled—
immediately—and at minimal cost. In his speaking, writing and coaching
wont, Neil shares these turnaround ideas with owners of healthy businesses
who just want to ramp up their sales, if this describes you, then Neil
welcomes your call of email. His strategies can help you increase your sales
- rapidly - no matter what business you're in, of what condition your
business (or the economy) is in. You can reach Neil at 1.800.563.IDEA
(4332), or at ng@neikjodin.com.

TURNAROUND MARKETING with Neil Godin
CONT'D
What: My goal for growth for the coming year is to double my monthly average sales.
How and When:To achieve this, I will hire a personal assistant -freeing up the time I need to double my sales
efforts - by December 31, 2015. And, I will target 75% of my sales growth specifically on the ABC customer
segment.
Why: Because they represent the lowest of the low hanging fruit. (Also, because it's dangerous to have all my
eggs in one basket, I will begin to market and sell to customers in the XYZ segment as well, with a goal of taking
them to 25% of total sales by the end of the year).
How: I will start by holding a special event. We will invite prospective customers to a beef 'n beer lunch where they
can tour the plant; meet us, and see what we offer first hand.
M = Measurable:
Developing goals that can be measured gives you tangible evidence that you are accomplishing what you set out to do - or
that you need to revisit your goals and your plans for achieving them. Most S.M.A.R.T. goals can be measured as a whole,
and by components as well. It can be helpful to describe the current status of an initiative in order to establish a
benchmark (e.g. last year's home show produced ten sales; this year's goal is twenty sales).
A = Achievable
While they should be challenging your goals must be achievable, or you will quickly abandon them and simply carry on
with business as usual. One key to success is to think consciously about the resources you will need - time, money,
equipment, knowledge, skills, personnel, etc - to achieve your goals. Goals that are challenging but achievable motivate us
- while unachievable goals de-motivate us (think of all those broken New Year resolutions).
To ensure they are achievable, test your goals. Be realistic - list the obstacles that you can foresee - and how you can
overcome them. Again, think of the resources you will need - the time, the money, the knowledge and skill, the
equipment and the personnel that may be required.
R = Results-oriented
S.M.A.R.T. goals measure results, rather than just describing or listing activities. Again, be specific about why you are
setting each goal; how you will implement; and what the anticipated results will be. Also challenge each goal by asking if
pursuing it is the best possible use of your time, and other resources, relative to the return on investment you anticipate.
Key question: "Will this be the best possible use of my time and other resources?" If not, think of a different goal that will
represent the best possible use of your resources. When appropriate relate each goal to the bigger picture - your main
goal for growth in the coming year, for example.
T = Time-framed
Deadlines provide us with a sense of urgency, which is vital when we're planning for significant growth or change. Establish
milestones for each major goal, and mark these with dates, and the specific achievement planned for each component.
S.M.A.R.T. Goal Test Questions
Goal:
1.

Specific. Why set this goal? How does it relate to the big picture? How will it be accomplished?

2.

Measurable. How will you measure success?

3.

Achievable. Do you have the resources needed to accomplish the goal? Is this goal important enough to keep you
determined and motivated to accomplish it?

4.

Results-oriented. What is the key result or benefit you will receive by accomplishing this goal? What are other benefits
associated with achieving this goal?

5.

Time-lined. What is the target completion date for this goal, and what are the time-lined milestones along the way?

So, there you have it. And I hope this quick review will move you to put on your planning hat. It's the S.M.A.R.T. thing to do.

SALES SUCCESS with L O R I RAUDNASK

Change
I was speaking in Edmonton in October and as I flew in the colour of
all the trees changing was beautiful. It made me stop and think of
how change can affect us and how we can manage it.
It doesn't matter what season we are in, change is inevitable. It's all
around us - the weather, the leaves on the trees, the change in our
Government and the economy. Change is constant in life and it can be
stressful (yes, even good changes). I have been in sales for the past 30
years and I have seen so many changes over the years.

••HNrtafWlMi.
lori

There are some obvious changes that most people in sales will recognize , like:
¥

We are not always looked at as the experts on product knowledge or pricing
because our customers can find this out themselves on line... so we have to be
smarter. Through the use of the internet, our customers already basically know
what they want and what they are willing to pay. This being the case, we have to
know our product, pricing, features and benefits inside and out to be looked at as
an expert. My daughter just went through the new vehicle purchase process and
in some situations she knew more about the features of the vehicle than the
salesman.

¥

The overall selling cycle may take longer these days (finding someone with
money). Due to on line research, the selling cycle for the customer is longer and
actually shorter for the sales person. By the time the customer comes in your
door, they are closer to the buying decision.

¥

Finding someone with money isn't always with cold calling or waiting for
someone to walk into your business. Finding someone with money can be with
the use of email marketing and through social media before you have an in
person discussion. A prospect's buying decision most likely happens before they
even talk to a salesperson. So the question is what is that customer reading and
where are they reading it?

¥

In the busyness of life more and more people are using online sales and the
product is shipped many times with no fee
right to their front door. I use to make the

coached, trained and mentored thousands of people around the world.

customer (where I would most always

over 100 million dollars in direct sales. For over 3 decades she has
make another sale) and I don't think that

conference and phone calls replacing that

¥ Product demonstrations can now be done on line via video rather than having to
read a manual. Consumers know how to use a product before they even buy
it.
¥ Sales people can learn so much on line to improve their own training.
•

An email thank you is more convenient and timely than a hand written thank
you card. Never underestimate the power of a hand written thank you card
being received by snail mail. I make Monday mornings my thank you writing
part of my week and I often get thanked more for the thank you card than for
my service.

Even good change can be stressful because it takes energy to do something new
and unfamiliar. Some people embrace change and some find change very fatiguing
especially when small changes gang up on you.
If you are not up to date with social media, take time to practice a little each day until
it doesn't scare you anymore. If we make social media and the internet our friend it
is a positive tool and it will help you grow your sales and business.

A n o t h e r i m p o r t a n t aspect o f a g o o d c o u r s e i s t h a t i t p r e s e n t s r e a l i s t i c g o a l s a n d e x p e c t a t i o n s . I f a c o u r s e p r o m o t e r
tells y o u that y o u are going t o get r i c h w i t h i n 7 days, I w o u l d be a bit skeptical. B u t i f they tell y o u that y o u w i l l
probably p a y for the course i n a f e w m o n t h s , t h e n that is a little m o r e realistic. D o n ' t get m e w r o n g here, y o u c a n
make really big profits really quickly, i f y o u put y o u r m i n d t o it and do things properly, but don't count o n it
h a p p e n i n g r i g h t o f f t h e start. A n o t h e r i m p o r t a n t c o n s i d e r a t i o n t o l o o k a t i s w h o m t h e c o u r s e i s m e a n t f o r . I s t h e
course appropriate for Canadians o r is i t specifically w r i t t e n for the U S m a r k e t and are w e j u s t a n additional cash
c o w f o r t h e U S m a r k e t e r ? I c o n s i d e r t h i s a v e r y i m p o r t a n t p o i n t as m o s t o f t h e c u r r e n t b o o k s a n d c o u r s e p a c k a g e s a r e
w r i t t e n a n d p r o d u c e d f o r t h e A m e r i c a n m a r k e t a n d as s u c h h a v e l i t t l e o r n o C a n a d i a n c o n t e n t . T r u s t m e , s e l l i n g f r o m
C a n a d a is v e r y d i f f e r e n t t h a n s e l l i n g f r o m t h e U S , a n d a g o o d c o u r s e w i l l a d d r e s s t h o s e d i f f e r e n c e s .
N o w for some o f the w a r n i n g signs I t h i n k people s h o u l d be o n t h e l o o k o u t f o r before t h e y b u y a n E b a y course
package. Firstly, are y o u p a y i n g a f i x e d specified price for the course up front only, o r are y o u being asked t o
s u b s c r i b e t o a r e c u r r i n g f e e s t r u c t u r e . I b e l i e v e a g o o d i n t r o d u c t o r y c o u r s e s h o u l d b e at a r e a s o n a b l e fixed p r i c e

As you well know by now, I LOVE using stories in marketing and sales. It grabs attention and
compiles them to buy. The best part? It's proven in all kinds of scientific studies that the use of
stories in selling grows sales by large amounts (one large study by Carnegie Mellon showed a 158%
increase in sales with the use of stories, vs using facts).
Pixar is a storytelling MASTER. As you work on your stories, think about these rules and how
them apply to you, the main character in your marketing.

BALANCING ACT with Randall Orser

Lessons Your Business C a n L e a r n f r o m Starbucks
Starbucks is the go-to business for picking up your daily Java. They put pumpkin
spice lattes on the map, and they even let you purchase bags of their premium
coffee to make on your own at home every morning.
Given the high-profile reputation they have obtained since opening their first coffee shop in 1971, it
should come as no surprise to know that there are quite a few business principles you can learn from
Starbucks.
1.

A cup of coffee makes everything better.

When Jerry Baldwin, Zev Siegl and Gordon Bowker were conceptualizing Starbucks, they likely knew
their idea was fairly unique, but what they didn't know was how high the demand would be. Coffee is
made daily in so many homes, it makes sense that people would purchase coffee beans and brewing
equipment.
However, about 11 years after the first Starbucks opened in Seattle, it was still only selling coffee-making
staples. The founders sold their business to Howard Schulz, who quickly took the business to another
level by introducing the option to purchase brewed coffee beverages in-store. He married the popularity
of coffee with the convenience of not having to brew it yourself, and Starbucks began to rapidly succeed.
2. Consistency matters.
Perhaps one of the reasons that Starbucks has experienced so much success is the fact that on any
day, in any city, you can walk into any Starbucks and get the exact the same drink. Starbucks utilizes
recipes, to which staff are expected to strictly adhere to unless something different is requested. This
creates an excellent experience for customers across the board.
Furthermore, they guarantee that if you dont love your drink, they will re-make it for you J/vith that kind of
consistency and commitment to excellence, it is nearly impossible to have a bad experience at
Starbucks.
3. Creating a diverse culture adds to your success.
Starbucks is a diverse employer with staff that come from many walks of life. Coffee shops have a
reputation for only hiring college students who are short on enthusiasm and riddled with angst. It is clear
that Starbucks has managed to avoid this stereotype when you can walk into any of their stores and see
baristas with a wide array of backgrounds, who are ready to serve you your daily dose of coffee with
plenty of courtesy.
If you are eager to make your business more culturally relevant and successful, Starbucks has your
recipe for success. Regardless of the size of your
business, you can create a unique, innovative and
consistent company culture using the same principles Randall Orser is President of Number Crunchers Financial Services
that Starbucks has already successfully
located in Surrey, BC. 'On time mobile bookkeeping services that
won't get you audited, guaranteed!'You can reach him via phone:

The Klondike Gold Rush...
what really happened to 30,000 men
- and how critical it is to your future
wealth, by Troy White

W h a t follows isa true story o f the Klondike Gold Rush.

This isa condensed version o f a fantastic reference b o o k I read called T h e Klondike Quest. I assure y o u
t h a t t h e r e a r e a t o n o f l e s s o n s i n t h i s s t o r y - t h a t a p p l y j u s t a s m u c h t o d a y a s t h e y e v e r h a v e . With a

On a chilly July m o r n i n g in 1897, the whispers

began.

TURNAROUND MARKETING with Neil Godin
This month: Recession yes? Recession no? Who cares!
Like everyone else I listen to and watch the economic news. Right now, the news in Canada is mixed when it
comes to the economy. The Bank of Canada says we are officially in a recession. Alberta (as we all know) is in
a "deep" recession. Industrial Ontario is in a seemingly permanent downturn. The Atlantic provinces can't
remember the last upturn (okay, Newfoundland had a big upswing with oil, while it lasted). And my clients, in
all these provinces and regions, ask the same questions, again and again: " W h e r e a r e w e ? W h e r e a r e w e g o i n g ?
When does this g e t b e t t e r ? " Even here in Vancouver - where housing prices are making renters out of buyers - in a
crazy, twisted market all our own - clients ask, "When
will this b e o v e r - a n d w h a t do I d o in t h e m e a n t i m e ? "
My answer is always the same: "let's ask the 'right' questions." Instead of focusing on the economy at large and
asking (or thinking about) where it's going - let's ask ourselves what we can do to create "our own economy."
Instead of thinking about "when things will get better," let's ask ourselves, "how can I make things better-for me right now?" Changing our questions in this way has a dramatic, liberating effect - because thinking about "what we
can do," instead of "what is happening to us," can literally set us free, get us "unstuck" and help us feel more "in
control" when events seem to be spinning out of control.
This month, I want to share with you some of the advice and recommendations that I offer my clients (who
sometimes listen). Here we go...
1. Here are my comments about the economy:

*

»

In order to focus on building business - instead of worrying and wondering if the economy is going to
improve - 1 always offer my take on the economy, as follows: "When a market is down - even by 50% - it
means 50% of prospects are still ready, willing and able to buy - now!"
That's a huge number of prospective customers - and the number is even larger when you consider that
our Canadian economy is in recovery, and markets aren't down anywhere near 50%.
And - even if the situation deteriorates to the point that Canada is dragged back into total recession, our
markets still aren't likely to be down that much.
But here's the real point: Why should we care? You and I are powerless to influence "The Big Economy," so
why should we drag ourselves down by even thinking about it?
Instead, why don't we focus on "the other 50% (+)," the people out there who are ready, willing and able to
buy right now? And why don't we swing into marketing and sales action - right now?
If we do this, we will take control of the only economy we have any power to control - "our own economy."
While others worry (and wait for the phone to ring) - we'll be out there drumming up business and
enjoying a great economy - of our own making!

2. Here is a summary of our strategy for identifying and reaching "the other 50%"
Success in a tough economy is as simple as "1-2-3."
#1 - Identify "who you are" and "why I should care."
Describe in words how you are different and better than
anyone else, in terms of being of real value to your customers.
(By "value," I mean how do you help customers solve their most
painful problem(s) in relation to what you offer? Ask yourself,
"Where do they hurt the most, and where do I - or could I help the most?")
Here's an example: A computer service firm, right here in
Vancouver, actually paid attention to customers who were
almost in tears when they heard that they had to give up their
computer(s) for at least two days while they were being
repaired.

Former business journalist, Neil Godin (a.k.a. The Turnaround Guy®) is publisher o f Marketing Dangerously," the world's only marketing and sales "idea
service" for business builders, and author of "Selling in the (Comfort)
Zone" (available at Amazon and other outlets). As a speaker Neil has
presented to more than 300,000 business people from coast to coast in
Canada and the United States. As a marketing and sales consultant and
coach, he has worked with many major companies, including Shell, Ford,
The Royal Bank, Telus, Dun & Bradstreet, Subway and McDonalds, but
works mainly with smaller independ- ent businesses - and he specializes in
turnaround marketing work with small to mid-size companies in crisis. In
these turnaround cases, sales always have to be doubled or tripled—
immediately—and at minimal cost. In his speaking, writing and coaching
work, Neil shares these turnaround ideas with owners of healthy businesses
who just want to ramp up their sales. If this describes you, then Neil
welcomes your call or email. His strategies can help you increase your sales
- rapidly - no matter what business you're in, or what condition your
business (or the economy) is in. You can reach Neil at 1.800.563.IDEA
(43321 or at ng@negqodin.com.

TURNAROUND MARKETING with Neil Godin - CONT'D

Simple Solution: They started a remote service program, where your computer doesn't have to leave
your home or office at all. As you know, this is an approach where the technician takes over your
computer - online - and solves the problem from their shop. An email notification campaign gave
them an immediate burst of business.
At the same time, they started a "loaner" program, meaning that if your computer problem can't be solved by
remote service, they now provide a free loaner machine(s) that you can use until your computer is returned.
Both these ideas instantly elevated them way above their competitors and attracted brand new business to
them - as clients brought them their business, and shared the word. While I congratulated them on
implementing this simple creative strategy I cautioned them not to be complacent - as competitors could be
counted on to replicate their program. (Key point is that you must "maintain" a genuine competitive advantage.
How? By non-stop prduct and service innovation - based "exactly" on customers' deepest hurts, needs, and
wishes - so you are "always" ahead of the crowd.)
# 2 - Identify "who cares."
Ask yourself, "Who hurts the most....where you can help the most? In our example, this could mean
solopreneurs who own just one personal computer (desktop or laptop), that they absolutely can not be without
- even for a single day. Or perhaps a courier service with five or ten computers - all of which need to be
operating every second, or their business is in crisis.
#3 - Identify ways to get these prospects into your customer base.
Brainstorm the fastest, easiest and least expensive ways to get in front of your best prospects; attract them to
you - and convert them into customers.
•
In this process, keep focusing on "the lowest of the lowest hanging fruit." Which means attracting those
who:
Are most likely to get the greatest possible benefit from dealing with you
Are near the end of the sales cycle and are ready to buy now
Are most able to afford what you offer (or who have virtually no choice but to buy)
Don't focus on old fashioned sales prospecting (don't throw the net wide, hoping that the old "numbers
game" approach will get you the sales you need).
Instead use laser-focused targeting (a rifle instead of a shotgun, a spotlight instead of a floodlight), aiming
most of your efforts on a smaller number of ideal candidates on your "Most Wanted" list
If you know the decision makers on your "Most Wanted" list, brainstorm the best way(s) to get their
attention. In our example, a simple email marketing campaign, targeting your ideal prospective customers,
could be tremendously effective. This could be done with a simple headline and brief message like this:
"We're listening. And we hear you. You can't be without your computer(s) for even a day. So we've
launched a brand new 'remote technician program.' This means that, in most cases, we can service your
computer from our shop, by sharing control of your computer with you, while we're doing our service work.
And, if the problem can't be solved this way - then we invite you to call us for a free pickup of your
computer - and delivery of a 'loaner' computer(s) from us - that you can use, free of charge, while we
repair your computer in our shop."
If you used a really compelling subject line (in order to make sure your emails get opened) - and if you
asked recipients to forward the email to others who would want to know about the program - then even
this simple approach could bring in the new customers you need.
The bottom line? Tactics like this are fast, free, and easy. All they require is brainstorming, action-planning
and implementation. And, of course, it's always the perfect time to launch a brand new service innovation
in any business, anyway - so why not yours? And why not now? If you do this kind of thing, you will create
your own economy - because you're asking the right questions - and delivering the right answers.
Until next month...

Happy Marketing - and - to hell with the economy !!

SALES SUCCESS with L O R I RAUDNASK

Root rot?
For over 20 years our family has gone apple picking with another family. It is
one of my favourite days of the year. We started this tradition when my son
Kyle was four months old and my daughter Megan was two years old. My
friend Sharon and I would then bake apple pies and apple crisp. After a few
years of not going due to all the kids being away from home we brought the
tradition back again.

tori

Now instead of four adults picking there were 8 and when we got to the weigh
station we had picked 117 pounds of apples, which cost $195.00! That will go
down in history for sure. I now have a grand daughter Kaylynn and it was her
first year picking an apple and it was precious. Out in the field as I looked at the beauty of all
the trees bearing fruit it reminded me of a story I had read years ago.
It was about a tree that produced an abundant amount of fruit and everyone marvelled at its
ability to produce a record harvest each year. The owner who sold his fruit at the local market
had become one of the wealthiest men in town and he was the envy of all who knew him.
However, as the years passed the owner spent so much of his time counting and selling his
fruit that he forgot to nourish the root. He became so prideful and focused on results that he
neglected to see the signs that the tree was dying. Then one day when the owner went to pick
fruit from his tree he was shocked to discover that the tree was barren. "How could this be,"
he asked? But when he inspected the root he found his answer. The root had dried up. He
was so focused on the fruit that he neglected the root. He wished there was something he
could do but it was too late. It was a lesson he would never forget!
How about you? Do you focus on the numbers, the outcomes and the fruit? Or do you focus
on the purpose, people, innovation, culture and root of your success. Always remember the
amount of fruit we produce is just an outcome and measurement of how well we are nurturing
our root. If we take care of our root we'll always have an abundant supply of fruit. Ignore the
root and say goodbye to the fruit.
When we get complacent in our business you may find yourself suffering from "root rot". Has
this ever happened in your business? Do you take your eyes off the important things like the
people and customers who grew your business? I believe it is critically important for business
owners to diagnose their organizations in the same manner as they diagnose their markets,
consumers and customers.
Business owners need to know where the strength of the company is and where there
are gaps.
Sometimes when we have "root rot" we can no
longer continue to grow in the same business and it
is time for us to move on and look for a new tree to
grow.
What is the root of your success?
As we finish the year 2015 ask yourself how you
can nourish your roots to have a fabulous business
in 2016.
Happy New Year!

Lori is an International Speaker, Entrepreneur and Author who has
coached, trained and mentored thousands of people around the world.
She has mastered the sales process building a team that generated well
over 100 million dollars in direct sales. For over 3 decades she has
dedicated her life to helping othersWIN BIG!
Lori is the host and producer of the T V show called Persistence PaysTV
and is the author of Persistence Pays — How getting what you want is
easier than you think. Find out more at www.persistencepays.ca. Lori
can be contacted at 905643-4693.

cold, and starvation - but they w e r e close - too close to turn back now.

T h e first b o a t s o f t h e flotilla s t a r t e d t o a r r i v e a t t h e K l o n d i k e ' s river m o u t h . A n d t h e y c o n t i n u e d t o p o u r i n t o D a w s o n
d a y a n d n i g h t w i t h n o b r e a k f o r a full m o n t h . M e n p o u r e d o f f t h e b o a t s o n t o t h e s h o r e a n d c o l l a p s e d w i t h e x h a u s t i o n
( 3 0 , 0 0 0 m e n m a d e it t h i s f a r ) . It was here that the most bizarre spectacle of the entire Klondike

phenomenon happened.
R a t h e r t h a n r u s h i n g o f f h e a d l o n g f o r t h e g o l d c r e e k s , w h i c h t h e y h a d c o m e for, they did n o t h i n g . T h o u s a n d s o f m e n
started t o w a n d e r a r o u n d aimlessly. T h e y a p p e a r e d dazed, confused, listless - a n d w i t h o u t direction o n w h a t to d o
next. T h e y w a n d e r e d a r o u n d for days o n end in a n aimless parade.
For whatever their reason - they had given u p o n the gold d r e a m - and w e r e n o w content to d o nothing. T h e gold
w a s r i g h t t h e r e f o r t h e t a k i n g - b u t f e w m e n w e n t a f t e r it.
How is this possible?

H o w is it t h a t t h o u s a n d s o f m e n ( a n d w o m e n ) c o u l d g o t h r o u g h
12 m o n t h s of torturous hell - o n l y to give u p a t the v e r y last step
of t h e i r j o u r n e y ? T h e r e a r e m a n y t h e o r i e s a b o u t t h i s ... b u t t h e
fact is t h e s e m e n g a v e u p o n t h e i r g o a l . S o c l o s e - b u t u l t i m a t e l y
headed home with nothing to show.
W h i c h brings m e to m y point.
Having w o r k e d with m a n y entrepreneurs in the past and having
a t t e n d e d a l a r g e n u m b e r o f h i g h - p r i c e d s e m i n a r s ... w h a t i s
h a p p e n i n g i n 2 0 1 5 i s n o d i f f e r e n t t h a n it w a s 1 0 9 y e a r s a g o !

heard from. S e m i n a r attendees that heard the s a m e content I

to t h o s e with gold in their e y e s .

a b o u t b l i n d l y - w i t h s h i n y little o b j e c t s g l e a m i n g i n t h e i r e y e s t h e m e r e m e n t i o n o f a n o t h e r s h i n y o b j e c t s e n d s t h e m r u n n i n g off
in a n e w d i r e c t i o n . T h e y h a v e n o c l u e o n w h a t it t a k e s t o g e t t h e r e . T h e c h a l l e n g e s t h e y will f a c e . T h e o b s t a c l e s t h e y m u s t
o v e r c o m e . H o w l o n g it w i l l t a k e - a n d h o w h a r d t h e y m u s t w o r k t o e v e n c o m e r e m o t e l y c l o s e t o t h e i r d r e a m . A n d t h e n t h e r e

f r o m m a k i n g e v e r y t h i n g t h e y h a v e d r e a m e d o f s o far t o c o m e t r u e . T h e y sit t h e r e - w a n d e r i n g a r o u n d - a p p e a r i n g l o s t w i t h

T h e 3 x 5 card s y s t e m . A timeless technique to create a storyboard behind y o u r idea. Starting with the m a i n story point y o u
w a n t t o c o v e r . T h e e n d g o a l y o u w a n t t o a c h i e v e . U s e o n e o r t w o s e n t e n c e s t o o u t l i n e t h e s t e p s i n v o l v e d in y o u r s t o r y w e a v i n g y o u r w a y f r o m start to finish. Ideally y o u h a v e a beginning, middle a n d e n d in y o u r m i n d before y o u begin. M a r k the
b a c k s of the 3 x 5 cards with guidelines s o y o u k n o w w h e r e e a c h point g o e s in t h e finished storyboard (the beginning, middle,
o r e n d ) . W h e n y o u f e e l y o u h a v e s u f f i c i e n t p o i n t s t o c o v e r i n y o u r story, s t a r t f l i p p i n g t h r o u g h t h e c a r d s f r o m b e g i n n i n g t o
end. Do this again, and again, and again.
U l t i m a t e l y y o u will s t a r t s e e i n g t h e s t o r y t a k e s h a p e i n y o u r m i n d a n d y o u c a n l i t e r a l l y t a s t e h o w it will t u r n o u t . G e t o u t t h a t
p a d o f p a p e r o r y o u r c o m p u t e r a n d s t a r t w r i t i n g . L e t it f l o w o u t o f y o u a n d g e t y o u r t h o u g h t s d o w n a s q u i c k l y a s y o u c a n w i t h o u t t h o u g h t t o s p e l l i n g , g r a m m a r , p u n c t u a t i o n , o r a n y f o r m o f e d i t i n g a t a l l . ... c o m e b a c k t o it a n d s t a r t e d i t i n g t h e f l o w ( r e a d it o u t l o u d f o r t h a t ) .

a b o u t . P l e a s e s t a r t t r y i n g t o t i e in s t o r i e s t o y o u r b u s i n e s s . Y o u r c u s t o m e r s will l o v e it - a n d will h o p e f u l l y b e c o m e o b s e s s e d

you w o u l d like to s e e discussed. T o y o u r success.

BALANCING ACT with Randall Orser
The Lean Startup: Trimming Bootstrap Fat

Nearly 75 percent of all new startups end in failure, and many new products
will tank soon after launch. The high rate of failure is often the result of
a startup method that builds a product it assumes people will want to buy.
Sometimes customer feedback isn't solicited during the pre-launch period, and the
company finds itself building a product no one will buy.
With the Lean Startup model, success isn't about discovering the right product at the right
time. Rather, startup success is a result of early customer feedback and consistent
product evaluation.
What's The Skinny on Lean?
The method comes from a cost-cutting Japanese manufacturing model. With
the Lean Startup model, companies get early customer feedback to see if their product will
sell. The Startup uses a three-step process that decides if and how to invest time and
money: build, measure, and learn. The goal is to determine if a market for the product
exists.
Nuts and Bolts PL 1
The first step is to come up with a Minimal Viable Product (MVP). This is a prototype of
the proposed product that will allow consumer testing to begin.
Nuts and Bolts PL 2
With the MVP completed, the testing phase begins with customer interviews and testing.
The company finds out what potential customers like or don't like about the
product. Armed with this information, they have a solid foundation to build on.
In some cases, the MVP i s just what customers are looking for. Customers are only
interested in a product that will meet their needs. It doesn't matter to them what stage of
development it's in or how long it took to build.
Nuts and Bolts PL 3
The third and last stage of the process consists of building the finished product. Based on
customer feedback, the company addresse s any
product flaws, then creates a better product. The ,
product will either be adjusted with minor tweaks I
®
or totally redesigned.
I located in Surrey, BC. ' O n time mobile bookkeeping services that
R a n d a l l 0 r s e r isP r e s i d e n t of N u m b e r Crunchers

BALANCING ACT with Randall Orser
Cont'd
Trimming The Fat
Lean Startup focuses on exactly how and where a company needs to invest its
time and energy. This avoids a tendency to become hung up on unproductive
behaviors. Team members treat failure as a learning experience. They move
on, pivot if necessary, and move ahead in a different direction.

Validated Learning
Lean Startup makes use of consumer tests to come up with a criterion known as
Validated Learning. Validated learning is the process of gathering and trying out
consumer response. The goal is to remove any parts from the product that cause a
negative customer response. As a result, customer response is the essential part of the
process.
In its most basic form, a startup creates a product from an idea.
Successful startups bring value to the world since ideas move society forward.
The startup or entrepreneurial process need not be just one huge, chancy sink- or-swim
model.
By reworking the product around customer feedback, success becomes a distinct
possibility.

TURNAROUND MARKETING with Neil Godin
This m o n t h :

Total Customer Satisfaction -

"Why?"

This month I want to focus on 'total customer satisfaction.' As you know this is one of my favorite themes for a very good but simple reason: It is the least expensive, most effective - and often fastest - way to ramp
up sales in 'any' business. In this article I'm going to use the example of a Canadian company in the home
finishing franchise business. In my work with this client, I've been stressing two imperatives that are essential
for their success:
1. Getting work done right the first time.
2. Treating any problem that interferes with total customer satisfaction as an urgent priority.
I encourage them to actually "look for trouble" in terms of identifying even the smallest opportunity to improve
product and service. Why is this so critically important? Because it is imperative that present franchisees are
delighted with the product and service they receive - so that when contacted by potential new franchisees they will
say two critically important things:
1. The business is profitable. You can definitely make a good living with this franchise.
2. You'll love the support you receive from the franchisor. They are fanatics when it comes to product and service
quality.
Obviously, in order to earn these accolades from franchisees, we need to constantly look for ways to deliver
products and services that go "the mile beyond the extra mile." With this in mind, I wrote an open letter to the
members of the design team, following our first problem-solving brainstorming session. Give it a good look, and (as
always) jot down ideas and actions that you can use in your own business. Ready? Here we go.
An open letter from Neil
Here is an open letter (in point form) that I sent to members of the design team:
"I want to thank each of you for your contributions and your patience during Friday's Design Team brainstorming
session. I thought the session was challenging but very productive, and I truly hope you agree. As I drove home I
continued to think about the session and I'd like to share a few of these thoughts with you, as follows...
We are now engaged in some of the most important work that I will be doing with you - the work of
ensuring absolute customer satisfaction.
This is where the rubber hits the road. If franchisees are totally sab'sfied they will speak well of us to
potential new franchisees. And if our franchisees' customers (homeowners and builders) are totally satisfied
they will reward us with similar good-mouthing - and with their repeat and referral business.
If either is not sab'sfied with us, we literally put our company at risk.
•
This is not an exaggeration. Because we've chosen franchising as our business model, and because people
contact existing franchisees when considering purchase
of a franchise, we can not afford a single mis-step when

TURNAROUND MARKETING with Neil Godin - CONT'D

Very few companies have a "customer-centered culture" where everything we do is primarily focused
on customer satisfaction (in the belief that satisfied customers will drive all other measures of
success).
In fact, sad to say, most businesses do things essentially for the convenience of the company - not its
customers. In other words, they're running their businesses upside down.
We need to turn this right side up. We need to focus on customers first...company second.
Let's keep thinking and talking about our customers. We need to ask questions like this:
o Do we do anything that wastes our customers' time?
o How efficient is our service? (Are we "on time or in touch" 100% of the time?)
o In terms of product quality, do we do it right the first time - every time?
o When a customer has a problem, do we react with a powerful sense of urgency?
o Are we asking our customers how they think we could improve?
For example, when an order is shipped incomplete (without prior warning), look at what happens to our customers:
o A second installation date will be needed to complete the work (think "waste of time," and "waste of travel"
etc.)
o
o
o
o
o
o
o

If the customer had to take time off work to meet the installers, they will now have to take more time off (will
there be a cost to them, financially?)
When the franchisee (or their installer) has to make a second visit, this can cost them their entire profit on the
job (loss of earned revenue),
The franchisee instantly loses credibility with their customer (credibility and trust are lost),
The home owner or builder instantly loses faith in the franchisee and our company,
The franchisee loses faith in us.
While the franchisee is spending extra time dealing with the present situation they are not able to work on a
new sale (lost opportunity cost),
The franchisee may not be able to collect quickly, and/or may have to issue a discount.

Every company I work with - in any business - deals with the same kinds of recurring problems that you are suffering in
terms of customer satisfaction.
In order to solve problems that interfere with customer satisfaction, we have to literally "change our minds" - and start
thinking (and believing, once we have experienced real success), that "every problem can be solved." And that "every
problem is worth solving."
There's a paradox at work here. When we look at recurring problems, there can be a tendency to think they just "come
with the turf."
For example, we talked about how a job can leave the shop in perfect condition, then get damaged as it's jostled around
in the truck. But allowing ourselves to think a problem can't be solved is a death trap - again, we literally place our
company at risk every time we allow one of these problems to recur.
The only solution is to attack every issue relentlessly - not accepting any problem as just "coming with the turf."
If product is being damaged in transit, then let's figure out how to pack orders differently and have a "second pair of
eyes" check the packaging and loading before the truck starts to roll. (What ever it takes.)
When companies think about going this far to ensure customer satisfaction, the most common complaint is "what it will
cost?" (company-focus instead of customer-focus).
My answer: Look again at the time it takes, and the hard costs, of making errors that could have been avoided. In most
companies far more time is spent on doing re-work than it would ever cost to have a "second pair of eyes" double check
the work that's done.
What about the pay off? Consider this: If all our competitors think of recurring problems as "coming with the turf," and
we change our minds to believe that every problem can and must be solved, then look at the huge (and invisible)
competitive advantage we give ourselves?

TURNAROUND MARKETING with Neil Godin - CONT'D

•

That doesn't mean it's easy. As we saw on Friday, coming up with workable solutions to recurring problems was
painfully difficult.
Perhaps you could see how people in the meeting sometimes became frustrated, a bit irritated, and fatigued, as we
brainstormed and discussed different possibilities, until we finally got consensus on solutions.
No matter how you felt, the point is that this work is challenging and requires a tremendous amount of patience,
and tolerance of other peoples' concerns and points of view.
Most importantly it requires the determination to "see it through" - to persevere until workable solutions are
found, and agreed upon - and are then quickly acted upon (whether it's a short term fix, or a longer term solution).
Obviously, a real sense of urgency about solving customer problems is essential - and I left the meeting feeling
confident that you have the determination to keep this going.
Now I can't wait until our next session - and hearing your feedback on how our solutions are working, and your
ideas for fine tuning those solutions that need more work.
This is a never ending process...but what a ride!

Thanks again, and see you next time.
Neil

T a k e a l o o k a t y o u r energy. Will y o u r e n e r g y reflect t h e s u c c e s s y o u w a n t i n 2 0 1 6 ?

BALANCING ACT with Randall Orser

4 O l d Lessons N e w Entrepreneurs C a n Use
B e i n g a nentrepreneur i s difficult and often thankless. F o r t u n a t e l y , y o u ' r e n o t the first
one t o g od o w n this road. Y o u ' v ej o i n e d a l o n g history o f people w h o h a d a n idea,
believed that people w o u l d pay for it, and founded a start-up based o n that belief.
O n e o f the best things y o u can d o ist o learn f r o m those w h o came before y o u . T h a t w a y y o u can a v o i d
their m i s t a k e s a n d g i v e y o u r s e l f a leg-up i n t e r m s o f success.
1. T r u s t Y o u r I n s t i n c t s
Y o u r instincts usually w i l l lead y o u i n the right direction. There's a no l d test-taking strategy that i n v o l v e s
g o i n g w i t h y o u r first choice. I t prevents choice paralysis and spurs y o u into action, w h i c h is i m p o r t a n t .
T h e fact i s y o u can o n l y spend s o m u c h t i m e t h i n k i n g a n d d o i n g research. G o w i t h y o u r gut. N a t u r a l l y ,
y o u should o n l y trust y o u r instincts w h e n you're n o t sure w h i c h o p t i o n t o take, but have e n o u g h
k n o w l e d g e t o figure o u t w h i c h o p t i o n s are better t h a n the rest.
T h i s can also be applied to people. I f you don't think they're being completely honest, or y o u feel a
supplier c a n g i v e y o u m o r e , k e e p p u s h i n g . Just m a k e sure t o change y o u r t u n e i f t h e y insist that t h e y can't
do more.
2. L o y a l t y C o u n t s f o r a L o t
M o n e y isn o t the o n l y t h i n g that motivates people, despite w h a t s o m e T V s h o w s m a y w a n t y o u t o believe.
L o y a l t y exists and that loyalty can enable y o u r business relationships t osurvive r o c k y m o m e n t s .
E m p l o y e e s , suppliers, and business partners alike are f u n d a m e n t a l l y l o o k i n g o u t for their best interests;
w i t h loyalty, they w i l l v i e w their interests as tied t o yours, e v e n w h e n things l o o k bad.
L o y a l t y i s a t w o - w a y street. I f y o u e x h i b i t y o u r s e l f as s o m e o n e w i l l i n g t o t h r o w p e o p l e u n d e r t h e b u s
w h e n it suits y o u , y o u ' l l never inspire loyalty i n others. K e e p promises and back people u p as often as
possible. T h i s also goes for h o w y o u treat y o u r customers. I f y o u p r o m i s e t h e m something, such as
frequent product updates and innovations, deliver.
3. T h i n g s a r e B e t t e r T h a n T h e y S e e m
A s a nentrepreneur, y o u ' r e g o i n g t o face a l o t o f pressure, i n t e r n a l a n d external. Y o u r partners a n d
investors w a n t y o u to m e e t certain metrics and produce the right results. F r o m w i t h i n , y o u face the fear o f
failing and losing e v e r y t h i n g y o u ' v e w o r k e d for, w h i c h can lead t o a n u m b e r o f sleepless nights. Y o u
might even find y o u r palms sweaty atthe thought o f a
struggle ~ i f it's s u c h a g o o d idea, s h o u l d n ' t t h i n g s b e
going well, o rdid y o u m a k e a mistake somewhere?

4. A l w a y s b e Respectful
Y o u ' r e g o i n g t o m e e t a l o t o f p e o p l e as a n entrepreneur a n d it's g o i n g t o get tiring. E v e n t h e m o s t a v i d
social butterfly w i l l w a n t a little alone t i m e at s o m e point, but alone t i m e is not a l w a y s u pt o t h e m .
S o m e t i m e s y o u have t o meet w i t h someone, e v e n t h o u g h all y o u w a n t t o d oissit ath o m e w i t h a m u g o f
cocoa. Despite this, y o u must r e m a i n respectful and responsive to everyone y o u meet, even solicitors.
T h e r e are benefits t o b e i n g p o l i t e a n d responsive, but that's n o t the p r i m a r y reason for y o u t o d o it. It's
easy t o start seeing people i n t e r m s o f positives a n d negatives and h o w t h e y can benefit y o u r c o m p a n y . I f
y o u forget that you're dealing w i t h people, y o u w i l l soon lose touch, not j u s t w i t h potential partners, but
w i t h y o u r customers. W h e n that happens, you'll have trouble deciding h o w to develop y o u r product.
T h e s e lessons are timeless and u s e f u l t o a n y entrepreneur, n o m a t t e r w h e n y o u start y o u r j o u r n e y . L o y a l t y
w i l l always matter, regardless o f w h a t industry you're i n . Treating people w e l l w i l l never go out o f style
and w i l l r e m i n d y o u o f w h o m you're u l t i m a t e l y serving. R e m e m b e r i n g that things are better t h a n they
s e e m w i l l let y o u k e e p y o u r c h i n u p and k e e p o n t r u c k i n g , e v e n w h e n things l o o k bleak. T h e s e are far
from t h e o n l y t h i n g s y o u c a n l e a r n from y o u r p r e d e c e s s o r s , b u t t h e y ' r e e n o u g h t o g e t y o u s t a r t e d .
