TURNAROUND MARKETING with Neil Godin
This month: Sales Closing: Don't ask questions that can be answered "no!"

Tired of letting sales slip away at the last moment? This month let's look at closing techniques that enable
you to end that endless frustration. Here is my three part closing strategy:
1.
2.
3.

Watch and listen for buying signals
Respond to buying signals with a "trial close"
Use "the alternative close" technique (assume the sale is closed, and offer alternatives in configuring and
fulfilling the sale)

As you know, buying signals are messages - transmitted by verbal and/or eye and body language - that tell you a
prospective customer is satisfied that what you offer will solve their problem or fulfill their wish - and they are ready to
buy. When buying signals appear, the key is to combine two critically important closing techniques: "the trial close" and
"the alternative close."
Again, when buying signals emerge, it is usually safe to assume that the prospect is satisfied with the fit between what
you offer and what they need or want. To test your assumption, you make a trial close. You assume that the prospect is
ready to buy and that completing the sale is just a matter of making smaller decisions between "alternative" ways to
configure and fulfill the sale (i.e. which "alternatives" will work best in terms of product and price options, and/or
which alternatives will work best in terms of shipping, form of payment, and so on). And you simply ask questions
about which alternatives they would prefer.
Do not "ask for the sale" in the traditional sense
Conventional wisdom in selling says we must be forthright and simply "ask" for the sale, but I don't agree. Let's look at
the reasons why. The following questions are examples of asking for the sale in the old fashioned way:

m

*

"Pat, i t looks like a p e r f e c t f i t . D o w e h a v e a d e a l ? "
"Can I w r i t e up t h e o r d e r ? "
"Well,

Chris,

w h a t d o you t h i n k . A r e you r e a d y t o m o v e a h e a d ? "

The problem with these old fashioned closing questions is that they can be answered "yes" or "no." So the fate of your
sale can be like tossing a coin - with you losing (the sale) 50% of the time. Why? Because asking yes or no questions
gives the prospect an opportunity to reconsider and delay their decision. This is when they say those hated words, "I'll
have to think about it" about half the time. Here is an example:
You: "Well Chris, w h a t do you t h i n k . A r e y o u r e a d y t o m o v e a h e a d ? "
Prospect: "It looks g r e a t - b u t I'm g o i n g t o h a v e t o give this s o m e serious
a n d give m e a s h o u t next Tuesday
o r Wednesday,
okay?"
You (silently):
"Ouch!"
In this case, asking a question that can be answered "no" led
to the prospect saying they have to think about it—which we
want to avoid at alt costs. Again, simply assume you have a
fit (if you believe you do) and assume they are ready to buy.
Then test your assumption with appropriate trial close
questions about how to complete the sale.
Key point: While you definitely want to ask questions that
bring closure to the sale, you want to replace "asking for the
sale" with questions that ask "how they want to make the
purchase."

t h o u g h t . Leave

everything with m e

Former business journalist, Neil Godin (a.k.a. The Turnaround Guy®) is publisher of "Marketing Dangerously," the world's only marketing and sales "idea
service" for business builders, and author of "Selling in the (Comfort)
Zone" (available at Amazon and other outlets). As a speaker Neil has
presented to more than 300,000 business people from coast to coast in
Canada and the United States. As a marketing and sales consultant and
coach, he has worked with many major companies, including Shell, Ford,
The Royal Bank, Telus, Dun & Bradstreet, Subway and McDonalds, but
works mainly with smaller independ- ent businesses - and he specializes in
turnaround marketing work with small to mid-size companies in crisis. In
these turnaround cases, sales always have to be doubled or tripled—
immediately—and at minimal cost. In his speaking, writing and coaching
work, Neil shares these turnaround ideas with owners of healthy businesses
who just want to ramp up their sales. If this describes you, then Neil
welcomes your call or email. His strategies can help you increase your sales
- rapidly - no matter what business you're in, or what condition your
business (or the economy) is in. You can reach Neil at 1.800.563.IDEA
(4332), or at ng@neilgodin.com.

TURNAROUND MARKETING with Neil Godin - CONT'D

The key is to ask "which way" they would like to buy, not "if" they want to buy
Here are examples of the two approaches:
a. Asking for the sale (incorrect yes or no question):

"Well, Chris, are you ready to move ahead?"
b. Asking about the purchase (correct trial close/alternative close question):

"Chris, it feels like you're really comfortable with the fit here. The big question is, do you want to
start with the basic program, or go for the full service option... ?"
Be aware of the role of emotion in buying
It is vitally important that you understand the role of emotion in buying. If you simply said, "Well, Chris, this package
meets all of your requirements, so why don't we get started on the paperwork?" you would be addressing your
prospect's logic. But that could cost you the sale — because most people buy on emotion, then justify their purchase
based on logic.
So it can be more effective to talk about the feelings involved. Using the example above, we might say, "Chris it feels like
you're really comfortable with the fit here. The big question is, do you want to go with the basic program, or go for the
extra security that comes with the full service option?" (Talking about "the extra security" connects with your prospect's
deeper feelings about this purchasing alternative.)
Sometimes it's possible to test the emotional connection that a prospect has with what you are offering, as a way of
eliciting buying signals.
For example: "Pat, what would it mean to you, personally, if that problem could be solved?" This question drills down
beneath logic and into the core of what really matters to our prospects.
While this is an emotional exchange - it is built on a foundation of logic. Logic is critical, obviously. You are logical when
you are pre-qualifying. Logical in making your approach. And logical in asking the interviewing questions that helped you
drill down to what really matters. But when you also elicit an emotional response, it's like icing a cake.
You know your logic is on target when you have uncovered a need or want so deep that the prospect expresses emotion
when confirming their interest in that alternative. Now you are closing at a deeper level - and you can be confident that
as long as you deliver, you will have a thoroughly satisfied customer, "if" you close the sale.
See you next month

the w a y d o w n .
T h a t ' s h o w e m p l o y e d people excuse their t i m i d i t y . I n reality, a n entrepreneur k n o w s the w a y , goes the w a y , then
shows the w a y to others. H e ' s not a n idiot. Let's t a l k about smart entrepreneurs that end u p o n top.
W h i l e the w o r d , " H u s t l e r " has garnered a bad reputation, and it's a n adjective the seething hordes are w o n t t o
ascribe t o c o n artists and s w i n d l e r s , I prefer t h i s one: " T h e d e f i n i t i o n o f a hustler i s a person w h o is aggressively
h a r d - w o r k i n g , w h o k n o w s h o w t o get a r o u n d problems, u s u a l l y i n u n c o n v e n t i o n a l w a y s , w h i l e collaborating w i t h
others."
Entrepreneurs hustle, and t h e y d o i t honestly. T h e y see w h a t others d o n ' t and d o w h a t others w o n ' t .
A n entrepreneur i s prepared t o l i v e a f e w years o f his life l i k e m o s t people w o n ' t so that h e can spend the rest o f his
life l i k e m o s t people can't. A n d t h e y ' r e n o t j u s t g l o r i f i e d salespeople; t h e y are t r u l y creative. S m a r t entrepreneurs
take risks, but t h e y take measured risks. T h e y are courageous but n o t reckless. T h e y ' r e n o t quitters and t h e y bounce
r i g h t back u p w h e n t h e y get k n o c k e d d o w n . T h e y are patient a n d persistent because t h e y k n o w that g o o d t h i n g s t a k e
t i m e : I t takes 6 m o n t h s t o b u i l d a R o l l s R o y c e and 13 hours t o b u i l d a T o y o t a .
E n t r e p r e n e u r s k n o w t h a t t h e p a i n o f d i s c i p l i n e i s f a r less t h a n t h e p a i n o f r e g r e t . G a r e t t J o n e s s a i d , " P e o p l e w i t h
h i g h e r I Q ' s are m o r e patient, t e n d t o delay g r a t i f i c a t i o n , a n d save f o r the future. A n d t h e y w o r r y m o r e about t h e i r
r e p u t a t i o n s . " M o s t i m p o r t a n t o f all, entrepreneurs k n o w that t h e secret t o great and lasting success i s leverage and
c o l l a b o r a t i o n , s o t h e y b u i l d s t r o n g r e l a t i o n s h i p s w i t h g o o d p e o p l e a n d a v o i d t h e p a r a s i t e s a n d p o s e r s a t a l l costs.
W h i l e e n t r e p r e n e u r s a r e h a p p y f o r w h e r e t h e y are a n d g r a t e f u l f o r w h a t t h e y h a v e , t h e y s t r i v e t o s e l f a c t u a l i z e , a n d
t h e y s e l d o m settle f o r w h e r e t h e y are; t h e y seek t o i m p r o v e t h e m s e l v e s u n t i l the day t h e y die, and t h e y h e l p others
along the way.
T h e y understand that " y o u ' r e either green and g r o w i n g , o r y o u ' r e ripe and rotten." That's hasbeens: ripe and rotten.
Entrepreneurs w o u l d rather hustle 24/7 than slave f r o m nine to five i n some employee prison camp. T h e y are
c o m m i t t e d and they take responsibility. A n d t h e y ' r e a l w a y s l o o k i n g f o r a better w a y . I have f o u n d a n excellent
system that really w o r k s .

2 7 . P i g g y b a c k o n c u r r e n t n e w s ****
2 8 . T i e i n w i t h s p e c i a l h o l i d a y s ****
2 9 . O f f e r a t r e n d y o r e x c l u s i v e n e w s e r v i c e **
3 0 . D o a s u r v e y ( m e d i a l o v e s t h i s ) **
31. Agree o r disagree w i t h a columnist o r consumer advocate ( m a n y will m e n t i o n their m a i l i n
their columns or reports)

Any one of those could be fodder for countless story-based promotions!
The key is to actually DO THEM!

BALANCING ACT with Randall Orser
5 Horrible Things Y o u M u s t Accept A b o u t Being A n Entrepreneur

There's a lot o f potential i n r u n n i n g y o u r o w n start-up, and that potential is probably
w h a t inspired y o u to become a nentrepreneur. W i t h hard w o r k and careful decision
making, you'll eventually achieve financial independence - i n theory, anyway. T h e
t r u t h is, there are a l o t o f horrible things about b e i n g a nentrepreneur that y o u m u s t
accept s o o n e r rather t h a n later.
Acceptance shortens the t i m e y o u spend stunned and increases the t i m e y o u spend s o l v i n g problems. H e r e
are five d o w n s i d e s t oentrepreneurship y o u s h o u l d l e a r n as s o o n as possible.
1. T h e r e is n oL i m i t t o L o s s
Financial risk is a g i v e n as a nentrepreneur. W h i l e creating a successful start-up w i t h little capital isn't
unheard of, the situation w i l l often require y o u to open lines o f credit and procure business loans to help
t h e c o m p a n y g r o w . S o m e t i m e s , it's the o n l y w a y t o h i t the m a r k e t before t h e c o m p e t i t i o n catches o n .
Y o u c o u l d easily lose e v e r y t h i n g i f the c o m p e t i t i o n bullies y o u out o f the m a r k e t o ri f y o u r product a n d its
iterations are p o o r l y received. D e p e n d i n g o n y o u r context, losing c o u l d c o m e d o w n t o h a v i n g t o m o v e
b a c k i n w i t h y o u r parents o r b e i n g u n a b l e t o p r o v i d e f o r y o u r f a m i l y . I f y o u can't deal w i t h that risk, y o u
may not b e cut out t o b e a n entrepreneur.
2. Y o u ' l l L o s e T o u c h w i t h F a m i l y a n d F r i e n d s
B e i n g a nentrepreneur isdemanding, not just o n y o u r m i n d and body, but also o n y o u r relationships. Y o u r
personal t i m e w i l l b e consumed w i t h reports and marketing campaigns and product development, leaving
little t i m e for y o u r friends and family. Eventually, you'll lose touch w i t h some o f those people.
It's u p t o y o u t o s t a y c o n n e c t e d t o f o l k s y o u c a r e a b o u t . Y o u c a n t a l k t o t h e m w h e n y o u b e g i n t h e s t a r t - u p
and let t h e m k n o w w h a t to expect f r o m y o u . You'll probably miss out o n a f e w i m p o r t a n t events, but y o u
can a l w a y s reconnect once the business is stable.
3. R e g r e t i s I n e v i t a b l e
Y o u w i l l m a k e mistakes as a nentrepreneur. N o one has ever p i l o t e d a start-up t o success w i t h o u t s o m e
heartache. W h a t l o o k s like a great m o v e can t u r n out t o b e a b i g blunder. Y o u ' l l h a v e t o say n o t o w e e k e n d
invitations f r o m friends because you've got to prepare
for a b i g m e e t i n g c o m i n g n e x t w e e k . Y o u m a y e v e n
regret h a v i n g become a nentrepreneur. W h e n the

regrets deter y o u f r o m entrepreneurship. T h e y ' r e j u s t

BALANCING ACT with Randall Orser
Cont'd
4 . You'll be Incredibly Stressed
E v e r y e n t r e p r e n e u r w i l l e x p e r i e n c e stress. S o m e days y o u ' l l l o o k a t t h e m e t r i c s a n d h a v e n o idea
h o w t o meet t h e m ; other days, you'll consider quittingbecause the pressure seems
unbearable. That's the trade-off for h a v i n g control. Y e s , y o u get to decide h o w the start-up g r o w s
and h o w the product isdeveloped, but that ultimately makes y o u responsible.

5. You're Likely to Fail
M o s t s t a r t - u p s f a i l i n t h e i r first y e a r . I f i n v e s t o r s s e e m s k i t t i s h , i t ' s l i k e l y b e c a u s e o n l y 1 i n 1 0
investments ever pays off. T h i s isn't a unique situation;this isthe history o f entrepreneurship.
People succeed despite the odds, and i f you're aware o f h o w tenuous y o u r p o s i t i o n is, y o u tend t o
be m o r e careful. T h i s m a y b ew h a t y o u need t o succeed. T h i n k i n g that m o n e y ' s g o i n g t o fall into
y o u r lap makes y o u complacent, and y o u m a k e e v e n m o r e mistakes.
H o r r i b l e t h i n g s s h o u l d n o t p r e v e n t y o u from b u i l d i n g a s t a r t - u p . K n o w i n g w h a t b a d t h i n g s t o
expect o n y o u r j o u r n e y as a nentrepreneur braces y o u f o r t h e challenges y o u ' l l face. Y o u can
prepare y o u r s e l f mentally, physically, and emotionally. W h e n the inevitable happens, whereas other
entrepreneurs w i l l collapse, you'll b e ready.

Million dollar business building ideas...
from a pizza joint? by Troy White
I a m a l w a y s o nt h e l o o k o u t for u n u s u a l m a r k e t i n g ideas people a r e using t o p r o m o t e t h e i r
business. M a n y times I see these wacky marketing ideas offline, and they can easily b e applied
online.
To m e , the opportunity offline isgreat ifdone

right.

T h e r e i sv e r y little c o m p e t i t i o n ( d e c e n t c o m p e t i t i o n ) i n t h e physical mail space... n o w c o m p a r e
that with your prospects email inbox! To you, this m e a n s the difference between 230 emails t o
c o m p e t e with... o r 1 o r 2 other envelopes i nthe mail box.
Yes, it costs more... but d o n e like this e x a m p l e below... not m u c h m o r e ( 4cents a h o u s e h o l d
with s o m e companies). T h e key isi ntargeting the right markets, neighbourhoods,
demographics, etc.

Here's how the pizza place did it...
Who'd have thought that a pizza take-out joint would have such s a v v y marketers?
I received a letter i n t h e m a i l ( n o t a d d r e s s e d t o m ep e r s o n a l l y , t h e y h a d b l a n k e t e d
n e i g h b o r h o o d s n e a r t h e m - hint). O n t h e f r o n t w a s a letter w i t h a s m a l l bag o fflour a t t a c h e d t o
it w i t h a s t a p l e .
T h e letter began... " D e a r Neighbor, W h y h a v e I a t t a c h e d a little tiny bag o fflour t othis letter?
Here isw h y : " and the letter t h e n goes on t otalk about their 'secret flour' the chemical
s t r u c t u r e o ft h e i r flour, t h e h i g h p r o t e i n c o n t e n t , w h e r e t h e y g e t t h e i r flour, a n d w h y t h e y p a y
m o r e for their flour than the competition does.
Not hard t ofigure out w h e r e t h e idea c a m e f r o m !

T h e o l d d o l l a r bill m a i l e r r i n g s a b e l l , n o ?

T h e y d o a n e x c e l l e n t j o b building their pizza dough a n d ingredients up, a n d p l a y d o w n
inferior ingredients the competition uses, which explains w h y they have "limp, often soggy,
pizza crust".

the

T h e y talk about h o w theirs is hand m a d e daily, i n - h o u s e , w h i l e o t h e r s f a r m i t o u t t o
outside companies w h o m a s s produce a cheaper, lower quality dough that s h o w s u p ready t o
bake.
Then they have a 1 0 0 % guarantee: " i f it's n o t t h e b e s t y o u ' v e e v e r e a t e n , w e ' l l r e f u n d
purchase price. I nfact, w h e n y o u stop b y i nt h e n e x t t w o w e e k s , I'd like y o u t o h a v e o u r
signature Caesar salad with your dinner ( m y treat)"
T h e n they h a v e a coupon a tt h e b o t t o m with t h e free Caesar salad and Focaccia
This i s brilliant. A n d w h y can't Y O U use t h e exact s a m e
Y o u can... e x c u s e s will n o t b etolerated

bread.

idea?

here.

TURNAROUND MARKETING with Neil Godin
This month: How to attack the problem, and protect the person, when
mistakes are made
H i g h m o r a l e - m a r k e d b y e n t h u s i a s m , p o s i t i v i t y , a n d w i l l i n g t e a m w o r k - is a h u g e f a c t o r i n e f f e c t i v e m a r k e t i n g ,
because it drives customer satisfaction, w h i c h in t u r n drives repeat and referral business. And. High morale can be
achieved at zero cost - m a k i n g i t a very desirable goal. But. All t o o o f t e n business o w n e r s destroy m o r a l e a m o n g
t e a m m e m b e r s , by criticizing t h e m w h e n mistakes are m a d e . This h a p p e n s unintentionally, a l m o s t always w i t h o u t t h e o w n e r
k n o w i n g w h a t they're doing at a conscious level, and w i t h o u t being consciously a w a r e of t h e consequences of this self-sabotaging
b e h a v i o r . I've w r i t t e n a b o u t t h i s t o p i c p r e v i o u s l y , in a g e n e r a l w a y , b u t t h i s t i m e I w a n t t o o f f e r a s e t o f specific h o w - t o ' s t h a t c a n
h e l p y o u a v o i d t h i s r e a d i l y a v o i d a b l e t r a p . I ' m g o i n g t o w r i t e t h i s i n t w o p a r t s . T h i s m o n t h I'll s t a r t w i t h P a r t O n e : H o w t o p l a n y o u r
approach w h e n y o u need t o speak w i t h s o m e o n e about a mistake they've made. Next m o n t h : Part T w o : H o w t o approach t h e
o t h e r person w i t h great care. Ready? Here w e go:
Part One: Plan your approach
•

Reality Check. F i r s t , r e a l i z e t h a t y o u c a n ' t c r i t i c i z e a n o t h e r p e r s o n w i t h o u t f i r s t m a k i n g a n e g a t i v e a s s u m p t i o n a b o u t t h e i r
intention - a n d / o r a negative assumption a b o u t their character, c o m p e t e n c e or level o f c o m m i t m e n t .

•

Criticism is an attack. K n o w t h a t e v e r y f o r m o f c r i t i c i s m , n o m a t t e r h o w w e l l i n t e n d e d , is r e c e i v e d a s a n " a t t a c k " b y t h e o t h e r
p e r s o n - w h o can a l w a y s b e e x p e c t e d t o " d e f e n d " ( t o b e d e f e n s i v e ) . It's j u s t h u m a n n a t u r e . If y o u d o n ' t w a n t t h e o t h e r
p e r s o n t o b e defensive, d o n ' t attack. D o n ' t criticize. D o n ' t p r o v o k e defensiveness, it's as s i m p l e as t h a t (?)
Don't let criticism get in the way of consultation. A g a i n , c r i t i c i s m is r e c e i v e d a s a n a t t a c k b e c a u s e y o u c a n ' t c r i t i c i z e w i t h o u t
first m a k i n g a negative a s s u m p t i o n - e v e n t h o u g h y o u h a v e n ' t c o n s u l t e d t h e o t h e r p e r s o n as t o w h y t h e m i s t a k e w a s m a d e o r w h y t h e w o r k w a s d o n e t h e w a y i t w a s . A s a result y o u r critical a p p r o a c h c o u l d be o n t h e w r o n g track c o m p l e t e l y .
C o n s u l t a t i o n is e s s e n t i a l i n w i n - w i n p r o b l e m s o l v i n g .

•

Plan to use collaborative problem solving. C r i t i c i s m d e s t r o y s c o m m u n i c a t i o n a n d t h e p o s s i b i l i t y o f c o l l a b o r a t i o n - m e a n i n g
j o i n t o w n e r s h i p o f a p r o b l e m a n d its s o l u t i o n . C o l l a b o r a t i n g (vs. dictating) leads t o b e t t e r q u a l i t y a n d m o r e s u s t a i n a b l e
solutions.
Attacking is normal. U n d e r s t a n d t h a t w h i l e c r i t i c i z i n g ( a t t a c k i n g ) is s o c o m m o n i t c a n b e c o n s i d e r e d " n o r m a l , " t h i s c o u n t e r p r o d u c t i v e , s e l f - s a b o t a g i n g b e h a v i o r is t o b e a v o i d e d a t a l l c o s t - b e c a u s e y o u a r e a t t a c k i n g " t h e p e r s o n " i n s t e a d o f " t h e
problem."
Plan to create a "new normal" w h e r e y o u a t t a c k t h e p r o b l e m , w h i l e p r o t e c t i n g t h e p e r s o n a n d t h e r e l a t i o n s h i p . T h i s is n o t
easy; i t goes against t h e grain o f o u r conditioning, and requires b o t h de-learning and n e w learning.

•

Use problems as opportunities to strengthen, not weaken, relationships. S a d l y , m o s t p e o p l e i n a u t h o r i t y t r e a t m i s t a k e s a n d
p r o b l e m s as o p p o r t u n i t i e s t o fault-find, b l a m e a n d criticize - i n s t e a d o f o p p o r t u n i t i e s t o s t r e n g t h e n relationships, a n d
e n h a n c e p e r f o r m a n c e . In d o i n g so, t h e y w a s t e a h u g e o p p o r t u n i t y t o help t h e m s e l v e s a n d o t h e r s t o learn, g r o w a n d b e c o m e
m o r e cohesive. A s i m p l e t r u t h : mistakes a n d p r o b l e m s tell us w h e r e a n d h o w w e can i m p r o v e . T h e y t r u l y a r e o p p o r t u n i t i e s .
Connect the dots. M a k e t h e c o n n e c t i o n b e t w e e n e a c h p h a s e o f t h e c r i t i c i s m c y c l e :
-»

A m i s t a k e is m a d e

-*

Initial negative a s s u m p t i o n / j u d g m e n t

-»

Attacking behavior (fault-finding, blame and
criticism)

-»

Defending (defensive) behavior, including
excuse-making, denial, avoiding, and blaming
others or "circumstances beyond m y
control" (and/or counter-attack; a n d / o r passive
aggressive behavior)

Make positive assumptions. W h e n a m i s t a k e is m a d e t r a i n y o u r s e l f t o m a k e a " p o s i t i v e a s s u m p t i o n " a b o u t t h e p e r s o n ' s
intention.
No one wants to make mistakes. B e a r i n m i n d t h a t n o o n e o n y o u r t e a m i n t e n d s t o m a k e a m i s t a k e . E v e r y o n e w a n t s t o
d o things w e l l , w a n t s t o c o n t r i b u t e t o t h e organization's success, a n d feels terrible w h e n t h e y do m a k e a mistake.
Mistakes are made because we're human; b e c a u s e w e ' r e m o v i n g f a s t a n d t r y i n g h a r d , a n d u s u a l l y b e c a u s e o f
miscommunication.
Empathize with the other person. T r y t o i m a g i n e w h a t t h e s i t u a t i o n l o o k s l i k e f r o m t h e i r p o i n t o f v i e w . D i d t h e y g e t c l e a r
i n s t r u c t i o n s ? W e r e t h e y pulled in several directions? Did t h e y h a v e t h e k n o w l e d g e , skill, a n d resources n e e d e d t o d o t h e
j o b correctly? Did t h e y start doing t h e task t h e w a y t h e y w e r e taught, a n d t h e n discover a better w a y ? (Keep y o u r m i n d
o p e n t o all possibilities.)
Look for personal responsibility. A s k y o u r s e l f i f y o u w e r e r e s p o n s i b l e i n a n y w a y f o r w h a t h a s h a p p e n e d , a n d o w n y o u r
p a r t o f t h e p r o b l e m , (e.g. W h o h i r e d t h i s p e r s o n ? W h o t r a i n e d t h e m ? W h o d e l e g a t e d o r c o a c h e d t h e t a s k t h a t w a s d o n e
incorrectly?)
Avoid "drive-by delegation." If y o u d e l e g a t e d t h e t a s k t h a t w a s d o n e i n c o r r e c t l y , a s k y o u r s e l f , " W a s I g u i l t y o f d r i v e - b y
delegation - or did I take t h e t i m e t o delegate effectively?"

•

Ask instead of assuming. W h e n y o u a p p r o a c h , d o s o " c l e a n a n d c l e a r " b y u s i n g " h o n e s t i n q u i r y . " I n s t e a d o f a s s u m i n g
a n y t h i n g , b e p r e p a r e d t o a s k t h e o t h e r p e r s o n — h o n e s t l y a n d w i t h o u t p r e - j u d g i n g — w h a t is h a p p e n i n g f r o m t h e i r p o i n t
of view.
Don't buy into one side of a story. W e o f t e n l e a r n o f a m i s t a k e o r p r o b l e m f r o m a t h i r d p a r t y , w h o m a y v e r y w e l l g i v e u s a
v e r s i o n o f e v e n t s t h a t is v e r y d i f f e r e n t f r o m w h a t w e w o u l d h e a r i f w e c o n s u l t e d t h e p e r s o n w h o d i d t h e w o r k . If w e ' r e
n o t c a r e f u l , w e m a y t a k e t h i s v e r s i o n o f e v e n t s as t h e t r u t h , a n d p r o c e e d accordingly, m a k i n g conflict a l m o s t c e r t a i n .
Ask for help. A s k i n g f o r h e l p is a g r e a t w a y t o a n t i c i p a t e a n d p r e - e m p t a n e g a t i v e r e a c t i o n . T h i s m e a n s t h a t y o u d o n ' t
m a k e a n y a s s u m p t i o n or j u d g m e n t in advance. You s i m p l y tell t h e o t h e r person o f y o u r c o n c e r n ; and ask for t h e i r help i n
clarifying and solving the problem.
Be open to learning instead of correcting. B e p r e p a r e d t o a c k n o w l e d g e t h a t t h e y m a y n o t h a v e m a d e a m i s t a k e a t a l l t h e y m a y have tried doing t h e w o r k in t h e w a y t h e y w e r e coached, but t h e n discovered an approach t h a t w a s m o r e
effective (be prepared t o learn, instead of correct).
Suspend judgment. R e m e m b e r t h a t y o u c a n n o t k n o w , i n a d v a n c e , e x a c t l y w h y o r h o w a p r o b l e m o c c u r r e d . B y k e e p i n g
t h i s i n m i n d , i t is e a s i e r t o a p p r o a c h w i t h o u t m a k i n g a n y n e g a t i v e a s s u m p t i o n .

•

Focus on what, why, when and how t h e m i s t a k e w a s m a d e , n o t o n " w h o " m a y h a v e c a u s e d t h e p r o b l e m .
Use cause and effect thinking. B e f o r e a p p r o a c h i n g , a s k y o u r s e l f : " W h a t e f f e c t d o I w a n t t o c a u s e " b y t h e w a y I a p p r o a c h ?
By t h e t i m e a n d place I c h o o s e ? By t h e w a y I m a n a g e m y n o n - v e r b a l (eye a n d b o d y ) l a n g u a g e ? By t h e w o r d s I c h o o s e ?
The bottom line: I t is s a f e t o m a k e a p o s i t i v e a s s u m p t i o n a b o u t t h e o t h e r p e r s o n ' s i n t e n t w h e n a m i s t a k e is m a d e . If y o u d o
so, y o u set b o t h o f y o u f r e e t o b a t t l e t h e a c t u a l p r o b l e m , i n s t e a d o f e a c h other. In t h i s w a y y o u can use m i s t a k e s a n d
problems t o strengthen instead of w e a k e n relationships - while solving problems m o r e effectively t h a n ever before - and
reaping t h e benefits o f high m o r a l e ; synergistic t e a m w o r k , and continuous i m p r o v e m e n t .

If y o u t r y t h e s e t e c h n i q u e s a n d f e e l c h a l l e n g e d , o r n e e d m o r e i n f o r m a t i o n o n a n y o f t h e s e i d e a s , r e m e m b e r t h a t y o u c a n a l w a y s
e m a i l o r call m e w i t h y o u r q u e s t i o n s . I d o n ' t c h a r g e f o r t h i s k i n d o f c a s u a l c o n s u l t i n g - a n d I l o v e t o h e l p , b e c a u s e I w a n t t o s e e
y o u g e t r e s u l t s . (I'd a l s o l o v e t o h e a r y o u r f e e d b a c k . ) M e a n w h i l e . . . s e e y o u n e x t m o n t h .

Have You Begged to Go To Prison?

W o u l d y o u , a n innocent person, w i l l i n g l y go t o the
prison and beg t o be locked u p for n o good reason,

y o u give up control o f your financial future and shun

w i t h v e r y l i t t l e f r e e t i m e , l o a d s o f stress, a n d a n d a

A n d then, w h e n the prison w a s full o f w i l l i n g servants
and skivvies, w o u l d y o u send i n y o u r resume and
attend meetings w i t h hard eyed prison

up?
W e l l , that's a l l a j o b really is: a jail. A n d so-called

prisoners i n jobs.
A n d w h e n k i n d , generous, w e l l m e a n i n g people offer
y o u a w a y out o f j a i l , d o y o u despise t h e m for n o t
j o i n i n g y o u i n prison, reject their offers o f f r e e d o m ,
and question their intelligence and the validity o f their
offers, i n spite o f the fact that t h e y a r e free, h a v e n o
debt, a n d e n j o y a lifestyle y o u d o n ' t e v e n a l l o w
y o u r s e l f t o d r e a m o f ? E v e n w h e n y o u get t h r o w n o u t
o f prison, d o y o u scratch at the door t o be let back i n ?
Perhaps this describes w h y those w h o have the brains
and t h e courage t o start t h e i r o w n businesses,
including h o m e based businesses, quit so easily t o
return to their jobs:
" M o s t f o r m e r inmates confront some measure o f fear
o r a n x i e t y u p o n r e l e a s e , e x p e r t s say. T h e y t e n d t o

The Power of Collaboration
I t o o k a p h o t o g r a p h o f a f e r r y , b e c a u s e i t i s a n a l o g o u s is t h e r e s u l t o f c o l l a b o r a t i o n . O n e m a n , a l o n e , c o u l d n o t p l a n ,
finance and build a ferry o r d o all the w o r k required to sail the thing, but w o r k i n g w i t h others, w e can accomplish
anything.
Jay A b r a h a m , o f o f m y m e n t o r s , said, " T h e greatest d e t e r m i n a n t o f greatness i s g o i n g to b e o u r a b i l i t y t o collaborate w i t h
others w h o h a v e pieces o f the p u z z l e w e d o n ' t . " I h a v e spent 2 9 years specializing i n the use o f c o l l a b o r a t i o n a n d
leverage for s m a l l business o w n e r s a l l over the w o r l d , and I use it effectively i n m y o w n business. H o w can this apply t o
you?
I recently w r o t e t o a friend, " I can s h o w y o u h o w to create a regular, reliable m o n t h l y i n c o m e o f o v e r $ 2 0 , 0 0 0 per m o n t h
f o r $ 1 , 0 0 0 . " H e k n o w s I can d o this, because I have helped h i m d o things i n the past u s i n g collaboration. Together, w e
can d o amazing things, but alone w e w o r k for m o n e y and earn a linear i n c o m e that is a l w a y s t o o little. W e sell our t i m e ,
w h i c h i s t h e s a m e as s e l l i n g y o u r l i f e , l i k e a l o w - p a i d s l a v e . C o l l a b o r a t i o n p r o v i d e s l e v e r a g e .
W e a l l have strengths and weaknesses, and b y collaborating w i t h others y o u can have a l l the strengths y o u w a n t and have
access t o a l l t h e r e s o u r c e s y o u n e e d t o m a k e y o u r d r e a m s c o m e t r u e . A n d t h e u s e o f r e c i p r o c a t i o n i n c o l l a b o r a t i o n b u i l d s
strong relationships that can last a l i f e t i m e . A w e l l k n o w n , successful w o m a n entrepreneur once said t o m e , " R o b i n , there
are o n l y t w o k i n d s o f people i n t h i s w o r l d : givers and takers - producers and parasites. C o l l a b o r a t e w i t h the producers,
the givers."
W e h a v e a l l m e t the narcissistic parasites that seem t o a b o u n d i n a society that fosters a sense o f entitlement. These
p e o p l e are a c a n c e r t o a n y b u s i n e s s . T h e y a r e c o l l e c t i v i s t s a n d t o b e a v o i d e d a t a l l costs. I c a l l t h e m t h e s e l f i s h s e l f i e
s p o n g e s . O n e c a n ' t c o l l a b o r a t e w i t h t h e m , a n d i t ' s i m p o r t a n t t o test p e o p l e i n s m a l l w a y s b e f o r e g e t t i n g i n v o l v e d w i t h
t h e m i n any significant manner.
I call c o l l a b o r a t i o n a Joint V e n t u r e , but i t is also referred t o as partnering o r strategic alliances, and y o u can i m p l e m e n t
a n d use t h e m a t a n y l e v e l w i t h o u t a n y r i s k o r cost. W i n / w i n r e l a t i o n s h i p s w i t h g o o d p e o p l e h a v e a l l o w e d m e t o r e t i r e
t w i c e a n d e n j o y a secure, stable, e n j o y a b l e i n c o m e . Because I a m f r u g a l and r i s k averse, I t a k e n o chances and I n e v e r
r e c o m m e n d that people do.
I c a n s h o w y o u h o w t o u s e c o l l a b o r a t i o n i n y o u r b u s i n e s s o r t o set u p a n e w b u s i n e s s t h a t b e n e f i t s f r o m c o l l a b o r a t i o n a l l y o u h a v e t o i s a s k m e . Y o u c a n d o t h i s o n a f u l l t i m e o r a p a r t t i m e basis, f r o m h o m e , r e g a r d l e s s o f y o u r age,
education, background, o r circumstances, and y o u can spend a n y t h i n g f r o m $18 t o $60,000.

NEW B O O K . . . .
T h i s m o n t h w e a r e g o i n g t o t a l k about m y n e w b o o k t h a t w i l l j u s t b e c o m e a v a i l a b l e b y t h e t i m e y o u
are r e a d i n g t h i s . S o I t h o u g h t t h e best t h i n g t o d o w o u l d b e t o i n c l u d e s o m e o f t h e b o o k s i n t r o d u c t i o n
here.
Y o u w o u l d t h i n k t h i s b o o k is a b o u t e B a y b u t it's m o r e t h a n that. W e use e B a y as a reference t o w h a t
y o u c a n d o i n t h e r e a l w o r l d . E v e n t h o u g h w e t a l k e d a b o u t e B a y a n d e B a y auctions, w h a t w e are
r e a l l y t a l k i n g a b o u t i s i n t e r n e t sales i n general a n d s p e c i f i c a l l y I n t e r n e t a u c t i o n s . M o s t i n t e r n e t a u c t i o n sites operate i n t h e same
m a n n e r t h a t e B a y does. Y o u list y o u r i t e m s f o r sale, people b i d o n t h e m d r i v i n g t h e price u p , a n d t h e n at s o m e p o i n t t h e i t e m sells
a n d y o u get paid f o r t h e product. A l s o m o s t i n t e r n e t a u c t i o n sites h a v e s o m e f o r m o f feedback s y s t e m , s o m e sort o f e m a i l s y s t e m
a n d s o m e sort o f p a y m e n t s y s t e m b u i l t i n t o t h e m . W e w i l l t o u c h o n a n d discuss a l l those t h i n g s here.
I n t h i s b o o k w e w i l l t a l k a b o u t v a r i o u s ideas a n d v a r i o u s w a y s t o d o d i f f e r e n t t h i n g s t h a t r e l a t e t o I n t e r n e t a u c t i o n s . I n p a r t i c u l a r w e

y o u get t h e m . W e w i l l also t a l k about o n e o f the best w a y s t o m a k e m o n e y t h r o u g h i n t e r n e t auctions a n d t h a t is c o n s i g n m e n t

BALANCING ACT with Randall Orser
5 W a y s Entrepreneurs C a n F i g h t the C o m p e t i t i o n

C o m p e t i t i o n is i n e v i t a b l e as a n entrepreneur. E v e n i f y o u face n o o p p o s i t i o n a t t h e start,
competition w i l l pop out o f the w o o d w o r k , ready to challenge y o u r market dominance. I f
y o u r idea is g o o d , people w i l l i m i t a t e and iterate it.
C o m p e t i t i o n is healthy for b o t h the consumers and y o u r product, as i t forces y o u t o develop and i m p r o v e . A t the
same t i m e , y o u don't w a n t t o give t h e m a chance t o take the top spot f r o m y o u . H e r e are a f e w w a y s y o u can fight
the c o m p e t i t i o n a n d keep t h e m at bay.
1. S w i t c h D e m o g r a p h i c s
O n e o f the first things y o u ' l l figure o u t as a n entrepreneur is y o u r target audience. T h i s is w h o m y o u ' v e designed
y o u r product for. T h e y ' l l determine h o w y o u iterate y o u r offering and h o w y o u r m a r k e t i n g c a m p a i g n w i l l go.
Unfortunately, the competition m a y w a n t the same demographic. What's worse, they m a y actually have a product
t h a t suits t h e d e m o g r a p h i c better.
Instead o f slugging it out for that demographic, y o u can choose to s w i t c h demographics. Consider the advantages
a n d disadvantages o f d o i n g so. I t w i l l c o m e a t a cost, as t h i s is essentially a p i v o t , b u t don't let the costs dissuade
you. It's a g o o d source o f new business, and y o u ' l l l i k e l y still keep a n u m b e r o f customers f r o m y o u r o l d target
market.
2. I m p r o v e Y o u r C u r r e n t O f f e r i n g
W h e n faced w i t h intense c o m p e t i t i o n , this is probably y o u r go-to m o v e as an entrepreneur. Y o u ' v e established
y o u r s e l f i n y o u r target m a r k e t and y o u don't w a n t to g i v e it up w i t h o u t a fight. O n e o f the best w a y s to beat the
c o m p e t i t i o n is to s i m p l y b e objectively be better t h a n t h e m .
T h i s is best u s e d w h e n t h e c o m p e t i t i o n is i n t e n s e b u t d o e s n o t share y o u r l e v e l o f d e v e l o p m e n t o r resources. Y o u
c a n essentially b u l l y t h e m o u t o f t h e race b y o f f e r i n g s o m e t h i n g better. W h a t c o u n t s as "better" depends o n y o u r
p r o d u c t a n d audience. C a n y o u use better m a t e r i a l s o r offer faster service w i t h o u t c h a n g i n g y o u r price? D o i n g
t h i n g s l i k e t h i s isn't easy, b u t it's w o r t h c o n s i d e r a t i o n .
3. C r e a t e a L o y a l t y P r o g r a m
C u s t o m e r l o y a l t y is i m p o r t a n t t o y o u r success as a n entrepreneur, a n d it's i m p o r t a n t t o t h e c o m p a n y ' s s u r v i v a l w h e n
t h e c o m p e t i t i o n ' s k n o c k i n g at the door. T h e i r success, especially i f y o u h a v e m a r k e t d o m i n a n c e , relies l a r g e l y o n
stealing c u s t o m e r s a w a y f r o m y o u . D e s p i t e y o u r d o m i n a n c e , it's n o t that d i f f i c u l t t o d o , e s p e c i a l l y i f y o u h a v e n ' t
w o r k e d o n developing customer loyalty.
L o y a l t y a n d r e w a r d s p r o g r a m s are great f o r e n t i c i n g
people t o stay w i t h y o u r company. Y o u can a w a r d
discounts f o r l o n g - t e r m customers. M a k e sure y o u r
customers k n o w o f any programs you're offering.

4. O f f e r A l t e r n a t e P r i c i n g Structures
O n e o f the best w a y s entrepreneurs can secure a n advantage over the c o m p e t i t i o n is t o offer different pricing
structures. C y n i c s m a y t h i n k t h i s m e a n s l o w e r i n g y o u r prices, b u t that's n o t necessarily t h e case, t h o u g h i t i s a n
option. Alternate pricing includes offering p a y m e n t installment plans for b i g product o r large orders, o r n e w
m i n i m u m s u b s c r i p t i o n p l a n s f o r n e w c o n s u m e r s . T h i s m a k e s y o u m o r e flexible a s w e l l a s w i d e n s y o u r m a r k e t
reach.
5. T r y a N e w M a r k e t i n g C a m p a i g n
O n e o f the biggest p r o b l e m s entrepreneurs face w h e n the c o m p e t i t i o n starts p o p p i n g u p is that the c o m p e t i t i o n i s
n e w . T h e m e r e fact that they're n e w c a n t e m p t customers i n t o g i v i n g t h e m the t i m e o f day, w h i c h m a y b e a l l the
c o m p e t i t i o n n e e d s t o e n c r o a c h o n y o u r t e r r i t o r y . W h e n f a c e d w i t h t h a t t h r e a t , y o u c a n o p t t o f i g h t fire-with-fire a n d
try a n experimental marketing campaign.
W h a t part o f i t i s e x p e r i m e n t a l i s actually u n i m p o r t a n t . W h a t matters i s that it's n e w a n d different. I t refreshes y o u r
i m a g e a n d l e t s y o u s t a n d o u t from t h e c o m p e t i t i o n .
C o m p e t i t i o n i s inevitable and i f you're n o t ready to resist disruption and secure y o u r advantage, y o u w o n ' t m a k e i t
as a n e n t r e p r e n e u r . F o r t u n a t e l y , t h e r e a r e p l e n t y o f t h i n g s y o u c a n d o t o m a k e s u r e y o u d o n ' t l o s e g r o u n d . T a k e a
l o o k at y o u r pricing structures and give customers m o r e options. Create a n e w m a r k e t i n g c a m p a i g n t o negate the
competition's newness advantages.
I f you're o u t o f ideas j u s t t h i n k o f it this w a y - t o keep the c o m p e t i t i o n at bay, a l l y o u need t o d o i s t o b e a better
entrepreneur and business than the competition. K e e p i n m i n d that this w i l l happen m o r e than once and it w i l l
h a p p e n constantly. There's a l w a y s g o i n g t o b e s o m e o n e l o o k i n g t o take y o u r spot.
